Why Time Cannot Be Made of Indivisible Instants
Proof by reductio that time cannot be composed of indivisible instants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reductio argument that time composed of indivisible instants leads to atomism, and why that conclusion is considered false.

Core Idea
If time were indivisible instants, motion would force matter into indivisible atoms—a false view.

This lesson examines a key kalam argument against the idea that time consists of indivisible moments. The argument shows that such a view leads to the doctrine of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard), which was rejected by many theologians. By tracing the logic, you will see how the structure of motion and distance forces a contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the logical flow emerge naturally.
The passage is a compact reductio; notice the conditional 'if...then' structure.
2
Identify the assumption and conditional
Find the initial assumption: that time is composed of indivisible instants. Then see how motion in such an instant implies indivisible distance.
The phrase 'لزم كون الجسم مركباً من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ' is the key consequence.
3
Trace the contradiction
The argument shows that if the distance were divisible, the instant would be divided, contradicting the assumption. This leads to the conclusion that the premise (time composed of indivisible instants) must be false.
The term 'خلف' (contradiction) signals the reductio.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الآنات المتتالية التي يكون كل واحد منها [ غير قابل للقسمة ] ولو كان الأمر كذلك لزم كون الجسم مركباً من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ ، لأن القدر الذي يتحرك عليه المتحرك من المسافة في الآن الواحد، الذي لا يقبل القسمة - إن كان منقسماً - كانت الحركة إلى نصفه واقعة في نصف ذلك الآن ، [ والحركة الواقعة في النصف الثاني من ذلك الآن ، فحينئذ ينتصف ذلك الآن ] وكنا قد فرضنا أنه لا ينتصف . هذا خلف . فثبت أن القول بكون الزمان مركباً من أشياء حاضرة ، كل واحد منها لا ينقسم، يفضي إلى إثبات الجوهر الفرد ، وهو باطل . فكان القول بوجود الزمان باطلا.
The successive instants, each of which is [indivisible], and if it were so, then it would necessitate that the body is composed of indivisible parts, because the distance that the moving object traverses in a single instant, which is indivisible—if it were divisible, then the motion to half of it would occur in half of that instant, and the motion occurring in the second half of that instant, then that instant would be divided, whereas we had assumed it is not divided. This is a contradiction. Thus it is established that the statement that time is composed of present things, each of which is indivisible, leads to affirming the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard), which is false. So the statement of the existence of time is false.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage presents a reductio ad absurdum argument against the view that time is composed of indivisible instants. It assumes that if time were made of such instants, then motion would require that the distance traversed in an instant be indivisible, leading to the conclusion that bodies are composed of indivisible atoms, which is held to be false. Therefore, time cannot be composed of such instants, and thus the existence of time in that sense is negated.

Key Terms
زمان
آن
الجوهر الفرد
خلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument proves that time itself does not exist.
Correction: The argument only disproves a specific model of time (composed of indivisible instants), not time itself. Many theologians accepted other models of time.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, what does the assumption that time is composed of indivisible instants lead to?
A) The existence of an eternal time
B) The existence of indivisible atoms (jawhar fard)
C) The impossibility of motion
D) The divisibility of the instant

Key Takeaway
The view that time is composed of indivisible instants leads to the false doctrine of atomism, and is therefore impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You live through each moment, but do you ever consider that time itself is a created, continuous gift from Allah? How does the falsehood of atomistic time affect your understanding of Allah's constant preservation of your existence from one moment to the next? Commit to reflecting on Allah's name 'al-Qayyum' as the Self-Subsisting One who sustains time itself.
?
If time were made of disconnected instants, your actions would be isolated snapshots with no real continuity. How does the fact that time is continuous reveal the unity and coherence of your life as a single narrative under Allah's decree? Write down one area of your life where you feel disconnected moments, and ask Allah to weave them into a purposeful whole.
?
The argument uses a contradiction to dismantle a false theory. In your own life, what comfortable but false beliefs about time (e.g., 'I have plenty of time,' 'this moment doesn't matter') need to be exposed and abandoned? Identify one such belief and replace it with a truth from this lesson that time is a continuous, created reality for which you are accountable.

No Present Part Means No Time
Proof that time cannot have a present part, leading to complete denial of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying a present part in time logically entails the complete non-existence of time.

Core Idea
Without a present 'now', time cannot exist at all.

This passage presents a profound argument: if time has no 'present' moment, then past and future lose meaning. The author argues that because past and future are defined relative to the present, their existence depends on it. Consequently, denying the present negates time entirely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the logical structure: first a claim, then definitions, then implications.
The passage uses short, precise sentences.
2
Identify the key terms
Spot the Arabic terms for 'present', 'past', and 'future' (حاضر, ماضٍ, مستقبل). Understand how they relate.
3
Trace the logical dependency
The passage states that past and future are defined by reference to the present. If there is no present, these definitions collapse.
This is the core of the argument.
4
Follow the conclusion
If no present exists, then past and future cannot exist either, so time has no existence in any temporal mode.
The conclusion is the complete denial of time.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this argument is significant for the discussion on time. How would a defender of time's reality respond?
This connects to broader theological discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني وهو أن يقال : إنه ليس لشيء من الأجزاء المفترضة في الزمان حضور ولا حصول البتة ، فهذا تصريح بنفي الزمان بالكلية ، لأن الماضي هو الذي كان حاضراً ثم انقضى ، والمستقبل هو الذي يتوقع حضوره وهو بعد لم يحضر . فكونه ماضياً ومستقبلاً يتوقف على كونه حاضراً . فإذا كان كونه حاضراً ممتنعاً ، كان وجوده في الماضي محالاً . وإذا كان لا يتقرر له وجود ، لا في الحال ، ولا في الماضي ولا في المستقبل ، امتنع القول بوجوده.
As for the second division, which is to say: None of the assumed parts of time have presence or existence at all, this is an explicit denial of time entirely, because the past is that which was present and then passed, and the future is that which is anticipated to be present but has not yet become present. So its being past and future depends on its being present. If its being present is impossible, then its existence in the past is impossible. And if no existence is established for it, neither in the present, nor in the past, nor in the future, then it is impossible to affirm its existence.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument against the existence of time. It states that if no part of time is present (i.e., there is no 'now' that is actual), then the concepts of past and future become meaningless because they are defined relative to the present. Since time would have no present existence, it cannot have past or future existence either, so time cannot exist at all.

Key Terms
زمان
حاضر
ماضٍ
مستقبل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time could still exist even without a present moment, as a series of past and future events.
Correction: The passage shows that past and future are defined only in relation to a present. Without a present, they cannot be coherently defined, so time loses all basis for existence.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, what is required for time to have past and future?
A) A present part
B) An eternal existence
C) A moving object
D) A vacuum

Key Takeaway
Denying a present part in time leads to the complete denial of time's existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You constantly worry about what is past and what is yet to come. But if the present 'now' cannot be grasped, where are your past sins and future plans truly located? How does this reshape your urgency to repent now, when this very moment slips away?
?
The passage argues that without a present, time is impossible. If time is an illusion, what does that mean for your attachment to worldly deadlines and achievements? Are you building your life on something that has no real existence?
?
Consider the 'now' you are reading this in. Can you hold it? If not, then your entire life is only a mental construct. Will you continue to live as if time is a container you possess, or will you turn to the One who is timeless and truly present?

The Dilemma of Time: Created or Eternal?
Proof that time cannot be created or eternal without contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the existence of time as an independent entity is rationally impossible according to this kalam argument.

Core Idea
Time cannot be created or eternal without contradiction — so time is not an independent reality.

This passage presents a powerful dilemma against the reality of time. If time were created, its own priority would require a time before time. If it were eternal, its changing nature contradicts the unchanging nature of eternity. This argument forces us to reconsider the very concept of time.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Observe the two-horned structure of the argument.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Analyze the first horn: time as created
Examine the reasoning: if time is created, its non-existence preceded its existence. This priority cannot be temporal because time did not exist. Hence, priority does not require time.
This refutes the idea that time is necessary for priority.
3
Analyze the second horn: time as eternal
If time is eternal, it involves succession and change, which require being preceded by another. But eternity (al-azali) by definition cannot be preceded. Thus, the combination is impossible.
The argument also adds a secondary point about an infinite regress of containers.
4
Understand the conclusion: negation of time
The passage concludes that the illusion of time as a container is false, and this necessitates the definitive negation of time as an independent entity.
This is the ultimate goal of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : إن هذا الزمان . إما أن يكون حادثاً ، أو قديماً . فإن كان حادثاً كان عدمه قبل وجوده ، وهذه القبلية لا تكون بالزمان ، لأن هذا الكلام إنما وقع في العدم الذي هو متقدم على وجود كل الزمان ، وعند حصول هذا العدم لا يكون للزمان وجود فقد حصل معنى القبلية والتقدم من غير حصول الزمان ، فعلمنا أن حصول القبلية والتقدم ، لا يتوقف على وجود الزمان . وأما إن قلنا : الزمان قديم . فنقول : هذا باطل . وبتقدير تسليمه ، فالمقصود حاصل . أما أنه باطل فلان وجود الزمان لا يتقرر إلا عند توالي القبليات والبعديات وهذا التوالي والتعاقب هو التغير وماهيته تقتضي أن تكون مسبوقة بالغير، والأزلي ماهيته تنافي المسبوقية بالغير ، والجمع بينهما محال ، فكان الجمع بين حقيقة الزمان وبين حقيقة الأزلية محالاً . وأما بيان أن بتقدير تسليمه . فالمقصود حاصل. فتقريره : أن القديم هو المستمر أزلاً وأبداً ، وكما أن الحدث يوهم إثبات زمانين متعاقبين ، حصل في أولهما عدم الشيء وفي ثانيهما وجوده ، فكذلك القديم يوهم وجود زمان مستمر من الأزل إلى الأبد ، حصل فيه ذلك القديم ، ولو حكمنا على الزمان بالقدم ، لأوهم ذلك الحكم وقوع ذلك الزمان في زمان آخر ، فإن كان هذا الوهم كاذباً ، فليكن مثل هذا الوهم كاذباً أيضاً في جانب الحدوث ، فإنه لا فرق في العقل بين البابين ، وحينئذ يرجع حاصل الكلام إلى أن كون الشيء مستمراً ، وكونه متغيراً - وإن كان يوهم وجود زمان يكون ظرفاً ووعاء لذلك الاستمرار تارة ، ولذلك التغير أخرى - إلا أن ذلك الوهم فاسد ، وذلك الخيال باطل ، وذلك يوجب القطع بنفي الزمان . وهو المطلوب.
The third proof: This time is either created (hadith) or eternal (qadim). If it is created, then its non-existence preceded its existence, and this precedence is not temporal, because this discussion occurs concerning the non-existence which is prior to the existence of all time, and when this non-existence obtains, time has no existence; so the meaning of priority and precedence occurred without time obtaining. Thus we know that the occurrence of priority and precedence does not depend on the existence of time. If we say time is eternal, we say: This is false. And if we assume it, the goal is achieved. As for its falsity, it is because the existence of time is only established by the sequence of priorities and posteriorities, and this sequence and succession is change (taghayyur), and its essence necessitates being preceded by another, whereas the essence of the eternal (al-azali) is incompatible with being preceded by another, and combining them is impossible. So combining the reality of time and the reality of eternity is impossible. As for the explanation that if we assume it, the goal is achieved: its exposition is that the eternal is that which persists eternally, and just as the created suggests the establishment of two successive times, in the first of which is the thing's non-existence and in the second its existence, so too the eternal suggests the existence of a continuous time from eternity to eternity, in which that eternal thing occurs. And if we judge time to be eternal, that judgment would suggest that time occurs in another time. If this illusion is false, then let such an illusion also be false regarding creation, for there is no rational difference between the two cases. Then the upshot is that the fact that something is continuous and that something is changing—even if it suggests the existence of a time that is a container (zarf) and receptacle (wi'a) for that continuity sometimes and for that change at other times—nevertheless that illusion is false, and that imagination is invalid. And that necessitates the definitive negation of time. That is what was sought.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument against the existence of time as a dilemma. First, if time is created, the priority of its non-existence over its existence cannot be temporal because time did not exist; thus priority does not require time. Second, if time is eternal, it involves change and succession, which imply being preceded, yet eternity (al-azali) by definition cannot be preceded—so the two are incompatible. Moreover, even if we suppose time is eternal, the notion of a container for time leads to an infinite regress or a false illusion, and the same reasoning applies to created time. Therefore, the concept of time as an independent entity is false.

Key Terms
حادث
قديم
أزلي
تغير
ظرف
وعاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is a real independent container that exists whether or not events occur.
Correction: The argument shows that if time were such a container, it would lead to contradictions in both the created and eternal cases. Therefore, time is not an independent reality; it is merely a relational concept.

Checkpoint
According to the first horn of the argument, why can't time be created?
A) Because priority requires time, leading to infinite regress.
B) Because the priority of non-existence over existence cannot be temporal since time didn't exist.
C) Because time must be eternal.
D) Because creation implies change, which time cannot accommodate.

Key Takeaway
The dilemma proves that time cannot be an independent entity because both possible origins (created or eternal) lead to logical contradictions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You live your entire life within what you call 'time' — planning, regretting, hoping, rushing. If this proof is true, and time is not an independent reality, then what have you been anchoring your entire existence to? Are you willing to reconsider every assumption you've made about past, future, and urgency?
?
Your anxiety about deadlines, your fear of aging, your nostalgia for the past — all of them presuppose time as a container holding events. The passage calls this an illusion. Today, can you identify one area of your life where you treat time as though it were a real thing, and then intentionally act as if that container does not exist?
?
If priority and sequence can exist without time, then your relationship with your Creator — your repentance, your obedience, your failures — is not bound by the timeline you imagine. What would it mean to repent completely in this very moment, as if the past that 'preceded' it has no hold over you, because time itself is not real?

Priority Does Not Require a Container
Proof that priority does not require a temporal container.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the priority of events does not necessitate a temporal container and how the argument uses an infinite regress to prove this.

Core Idea
Priority is intrinsic to events, not dependent on a container.

This passage presents the fourth argument against the necessity of time as a container. The argument begins with an obvious observation: yesterday's event is prior to today's. If this priority required a container, then that container would itself need another container, leading to an infinite regress. Since that is absurd, priority must be an intrinsic relation between events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the English translation. Notice the logical flow and the dilemma presented.
The passage is incomplete; it cuts off at 'wa yakūn'.
2
Identify the two premises
The argument starts with two known facts: (a) we know by necessity that yesterday's event is prior to today's, and (b) the prior cannot coexist with the posterior. Understand why these are considered necessary knowledge.
3
Understand the dilemma
The argument poses a dilemma: if priority requires a container, then that container itself would require another container, leading to an infinite regress (absurd). If it does not require a container, then priority is intrinsic and no container is needed for any events.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
4
Examine the objection and response
An objector suggests that infinite times might be possible, but the author responds that this would make the present day infinite, which is impossible. The response is cut off, but the reasoning is clear.
The objection is that infinite regress might be acceptable; the response shows it leads to absurdity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : إنا كما نعلم بالضرورة : أن الحادث الأمسي متقدم على الحادث اليومي ، فكذلك تعلم بالضرورة أن الأمس متقدم على اليوم ، تقدماً . ولا يمكن أن يوجد المتقدم مع المتأخر ، فإن كان هذا النوع من التقدم يحوج إلى وجود ظرفي ووعاء ، لأجله يحصل هذا التقدم، وهذا التأخر ، فليكن لهذا الظرف ظرف آخر ، ولهذا الوعاء ، وعاء آخر ، إلى غير النهاية . وإن كان لا يحوج البتة ، فليكن الأمر كذلك في سائر الحوادث لا يقال : هب أنه يلزمنا إثبات أزمنة لا نهاية لها، يحيط بعضها بالبعض . فلم قلتم : إن ذلك محال ؟ لأنا نقول : فعلى هذا التقدير لا يكون اليوم الحاضر يوماً واحداً، بل أياماً غير متناهية يحيط بعضها بالبعض ويكون
The fourth proof: We know by necessity that yesterday's event is prior to today's event, and likewise we know by necessity that yesterday is prior to today, in priority. And the prior cannot exist together with the posterior. If this type of priority requires the existence of a container (zarf) and receptacle (wi'a) for which this priority and posteriority occur, then let there be for this container another container, and for this receptacle another receptacle, ad infinitum. And if it does not require it at all, then let it be so for all other events. It cannot be said: Suppose that it necessitates the existence of infinite times, some enclosing others. Why do you say that is impossible? Because we say: On this assumption, the present day would not be one day, but infinite days, some enclosing others, and it would be...
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth argument against time. It begins with the observed fact that yesterday's event is prior to today's event, and that yesterday is prior to today. If this priority requires a container (zarf), then that container would itself require another container ad infinitum, which is absurd. If no container is needed, then priority is intrinsic to events and no temporal container is required for any events. The argument then addresses an objection: that infinite times might be possible. It responds by noting that this would imply the present day is composed of infinite days, which is impossible. The text cuts off before completing the refutation.

Key Terms
تقدم
تأخر
ظرف
وعاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Every temporal relation requires a container (time) in which it occurs.
Correction: Priority is an intrinsic relation between events; the infinite regress argument shows it does not require a separate container.

Checkpoint
What does the fourth argument conclude about the need for a container for priority?
A) It requires a container
B) It does not require a container
C) It requires an infinite series of containers
D) It requires a single container

Key Takeaway
Priority between events is an intrinsic relation that does not require a temporal container.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that yesterday is prior to today—but have you ever used 'not enough time' as a container to delay your spiritual duties? If priority is intrinsic, what does that reveal about your excuses? Will you today act on what you know to be prior, without waiting for a better time?
?
The passage argues that infinite nesting of containers is impossible, so the present day cannot be one of infinite days. In your own life, do you treat each day as one among an endless series, promising yourself 'later'? If this day is finite and unique, what priority have you been postponing that you must act on now?

Priority and Posteriority Are Intrinsic to Existence
Argues that priority and posteriority are intrinsic to things, not dependent on time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why priority and posteriority are intrinsic to contingent beings and cannot depend on an external time.

Core Idea
Temporal attributes belong to things themselves, not to time.

The author argues that the priority and posteriority we observe in contingent beings are essential properties, not derived from an external entity like time. This passage challenges the common assumption that time is necessary for temporal ordering. It lays the groundwork for a deeper understanding of causality and the Necessary Being.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Begin by reading the full Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall flow.
Notice the dense argumentative style typical of kalam texts.
2
Identify the main claim
The author's central thesis is that priority and posteriority are established for things in their very essences, not borrowed from an external time.
3
Examine the opponent's admission
The author points out that opponents admit that 'being after non-existence' is not caused by another, yet they still claim that priority/posteriority require an external duration. Spot the contradiction.
This is a key rhetorical move.
4
Follow the argument to its conclusion
Trace how the author proves that priority/posterity are inseparable from things themselves, and then links this to the property of the Necessary Being (not being necessary due to another). This yields the final conclusion.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question and try the activity to solidify your grasp of the logical structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجود، إلا مسبوقاً بالعدم، ولما كانت هذه المسبوقية أمراً واجب الثبوت لهذا المحدث لذاته ولعينه، امتنع أن يكون مستفاداً من سبب منفصل. وأقول: هذا اعتراف من هؤلاء الأفاضل بأن كون هذا الوجود موصوفاً بأنه بعد العدم، أمر لا يمكن أن يكون معللاً بغيره، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك، فكيف قالوا مهنا: إن هذه القبلية وهذه البعدية لا يتقرر واحد منها، إلا لأجل شيء مغاير يسمى بالمدة والزمان؟ وتمام تقريره: أن الشيء المحكوم عليه بأنه [ قبل غيره يمتنع تقرر وجوده إلا مع هذه القبلية. والشيء المحكوم عليه بأنه ] بعد غيره، يمنع تقرره إلا مع هذه البعدية. فثبت: أن حصول هذه القبليات، وهذه البعديات، أمور ثابتة لهذه الأشياء لذواتها ولأعيانها. ثم ثبت في خواص الواجب لذاته، وخواص الممكن: أن الواجب لذاته، يمتنع أن يكون واجباً لغيره، وهذا ينتج أن حصول هذه القبليات والبعديات، يمتنع أن تكون موقوفة على موجود آخر مغاير. والله أعلم.
Existence, except preceded by non-existence. And since this precedence is necessarily established for this originated thing in its essence and in its very self, it is impossible that it be derived from a separate cause. And I say: This is an admission from these honored ones that this existence being described as after non-existence is a matter that cannot be caused by another. And if the matter is so, how did they say 'Minna' that this priority and this posteriority are not established except due to something other called duration and time? And the full exposition: That the thing judged to be before another is impossible for its existence to be established except with this priority. And the thing judged to be after another prevents its establishment except with this posteriority. So it is proven that the occurrence of these priorities and these posteriorities are things established for these things in their essences and in their very selves. Then it is established regarding the properties of the Necessary in itself and the properties of the possible: that the Necessary in itself is impossible to be necessary due to another. This yields that the occurrence of these priorities and posteriorities is impossible to be dependent on another existing thing different. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage presents a nuanced argument that temporal attributes are not derived from an external time but are intrinsic to contingent beings. It begins by noting that every existence is preceded by non-existence, and this precedence is an essential property. Therefore, it cannot be caused by something external. Then it comments that the opponents admit that being after non-existence is not caused by another, yet they claim priority and posteriority require an external duration. The author refutes this by clarifying that priority and posteriority are inseparable from the things themselves. The conclusion is that since the Necessary in itself is not necessary due to another, these temporal attributes cannot depend on an external existent (time). The passage ends with 'And God knows best.'

Correction: Priority and posteriority are intrinsic to the things themselves, as shown by the fact that they cannot exist without these relations.

Ninth Proof: Time Cannot Be a Quantity
Demonstrates that time cannot be a quantity through classification and reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam proof that time cannot exist because it cannot be classified as a continuous or discrete quantity.

Core Idea
Time cannot exist because it cannot be a continuous or discrete quantity.

This proof from the kalam tradition argues against the reality of time by examining its necessary properties. If time had an essence, it would be a quantity—but both possible forms of quantity lead to absurdities. The passage systematically eliminates both continuous and discrete quantity, concluding that time cannot exist.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Notice the logical structure: a conditional statement followed by a classification argument.
The proof uses a 'if...then' structure to set up the argument.
2
Identify the two types of quantity
The passage divides quantity into continuous (connected) and discrete (disconnected). Pause and understand each definition before seeing why time cannot fit.
Continuous quantity shares a common boundary; discrete is composed of separate units.
3
Study the critique of continuous quantity
Focus on why continuous quantity fails for time: past and future are non-existent yet share an existent present boundary. This is irrational.
The key absurdity: connecting two non-existents with an existent.
4
Study the critique of discrete quantity
Time as discrete would require indivisible moments (atoms of time), which leads to atomism for bodies—a doctrine already rejected.
This proof assumes atomism has been refuted elsewhere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة في هذا الباب: لو كان للزمان والمدة ماهية وحقيقة لوجب أن تكون ماهيته هو الكم. وذلك لأنه قابل للمساواة، واللامساواة والتجزئ، ويمكن فرض جزء فيه ويقدر، وهذا هو خاصية الكم. ولو كان كمًا، لكان إما أن يكون كمًا متصلاً، أو كمًا منفصلاً، والقسمان باطلان، فبطل القول بوجوده. وإنما قلنا: إنه لا يمكن أن يكون كمًا متصلاً، وذلك لأن الكم المتصل هو الذي ينقسم إلى جزءين مشتركين في حد واحد بعينه، لكن الزمان منقسم إلى الماضي، وإلى المستقبل، وهما يشتركان في حد واحد بعينه، وهو الآن الحاضر، فإن الآن الحاضر نهاية للماضي، وبداية للمستقبل، لكن الماضي والمستقبل كل واحد منهما معدوم، والآن الحاضر موجود، فيلزم أن يكون أحد المعدومين وهو الماضي، متصلاً بالمعدوم الثاني، وهو المستقبل بطرف موجود مشترك بينهما، وهو الآن الحاضر، وذلك مما لا يقبله العقل، لأن كون أحد المعدومين متصلاً بالمعدوم الآخر غير معقول، وكون المعدوم موصوفاً بطرف موجود غير معقول أيضاً. وإنما قلنا: إنه لا يمكن أن يكون كمًا منفصلاً، لأن الكم المنفصل مركب من الوحدات، والوحدة لا تكون قابلة للقسمة، فوجب أن يكون الزمان مركباً من الآنات المتتالية التي يكون كل واحد منها غير قابل للقسمة، لكن ذلك محال، لأن القول به يوجب القول بكون الجسم مركباً من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ. وقد ثبت أن القول به محال.
The ninth proof in this chapter: If time and duration had an essence and reality, then its essence would have to be quantity. Because it is divisible into equal and unequal parts and division, and one can suppose a part in it and measure it. And this is the property of quantity. And if it were quantity, it would either be continuous quantity or discrete quantity. Both divisions are false, so the claim of its existence is false. We said: It cannot be a continuous quantity, because continuous quantity is that which divides into two parts sharing one identical limit, but time divides into past and future, and they share one identical limit, which is the present moment. For the present moment is the end of the past and the beginning of the future, but the past and future are each non-existent, and the present moment exists. So it follows that one of the two non-existents, namely the past, is connected to the second non-existent, namely the future, by an existent extremity common to both, namely the present moment. And that is not acceptable to reason, because the connection of one non-existent to another non-existent is inconceivable, and a non-existent being described by an existent extremity is also inconceivable. And we said: It cannot be a discrete quantity, because discrete quantity is composed of units, and a unit is not divisible, so time would have to be composed of successive moments each of which is indivisible. But that is impossible, because to say so necessitates saying that body is composed of indivisible atoms, and it has been established that such a claim is impossible.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth proof against the existence of time. It is a classification argument: if time exists, it must be a quantity, and quantity is either continuous or discrete. The proof then examines both possibilities. For continuous quantity, the problem is that time's division into past and future requires a present moment that is shared, but the past and future are non-existent, and connecting two non-existents by an existent is irrational. For discrete quantity, time would consist of indivisible moments (atoms of time), which leads to the problematic doctrine of atomism for bodies, which is rejected. Since both types of quantity are impossible, time cannot exist as a quantity.

Key Terms

مدة
كم
كم متصل
كم منفصل
آن
جزء لا يتجزأ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is about time's passage or psychological experience.
Correction: The proof is a metaphysical argument about time's categorical nature, not about our perception of time. It focuses on the logical absurdities of assigning quantity to time.

Checkpoint
Why does the ninth proof reject continuous quantity for time?
A) Because past and future are both existent
B) Because the present moment is shared but it is non-existent
C) Because connecting two non-existents by an existent is irrational
D) Because time is not divisible

Key Takeaway
The ninth proof uses a classification argument to show that time cannot exist because it would have to be a quantity, but both continuous and discrete quantity lead to absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof argues that the past and future are non-existent. How much of your mental energy is spent on the non-existent past (regret, nostalgia) and future (anxiety, planning)? What would change if you truly lived as if only the present moment is real?
?
You rely on time every day (schedules, deadlines, prayers). If time is not a real entity, what does that mean for your perception of waiting, of age, of the 'time' you think you have? How should this affect your urgency in worship?
?
The discrete quantity argument leads to atomism, which the author says is impossible. But modern science often treats time as discrete (Planck time). Does this proof challenge your assumptions about time's reality? How do you reconcile this with your daily experience?

The Fourth Proof: Time Cannot Be Motion
The fourth proof argues that time cannot be motion due to multiple celestial spheres moving at different speeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the diversity of celestial motions demonstrates that time must be a distinct container, not identical to any motion.

Core Idea
Time is the single vessel that holds all motions.

This lesson presents the fourth rational proof that time is distinct from motion. By examining the varying speeds of celestial spheres, the argument shows that if time were motion, we would end up with many simultaneous days—an absurdity. The proof concludes that time must be a separate measure common to all motions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. This allows the author's own reasoning to sink in before analysis.
Pay attention to the structure: premises, dilemma, conclusion, and strengthening.
2
Understand the celestial spheres scenario
Grasp the fact that spheres parallel to the ecliptic move at different speeds depending on their distance from it.
This is the key premise: multiple motions with varying speeds.
3
Follow the dilemma
If time were motion, then either it is one specific motion (arbitrary) or all motions (absurd). See why both options fail.
The absurdity of many simultaneous days is the central contradiction.
4
Notice the strengthening argument
Reason itself tells us that all these motions occur in one time—confirming that time is a container for them all.
This adds rational force to the conclusion.
5
Connect to the conclusion
The only way out is to say time is distinct from motion, a single measure for all motions.
This is the required conclusion: time ≠ motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : إن أعظم الدوائر الفلكية هي المنطقة ، وأما الدوائر الموازية لها فكل ما كان منها أقرب إلى المنطقة ، كانت حركته أسرع ، وما كان منها أبعد من المنطقة كانت حركته أبطأ . فظهر أن الحركات اليومية الحاصلة في الدوائر الفلكية المتوازية الموازنة للمنطقة الفلكية كثيرة ومختلفة بالسرعة والبطء ، فلو كان الزمان عبارة عن حركة الفلك ، لما كان جعله عبارة عن حركة بعض تلك الدوائر أولى من جعله عبارة عن حركات سائر الدوائر . فإما أن يكون عبارة عن الكل فحينئذ يلزم أن يكون هذا اليوم الواحد لا يكون يوماً واحداً بل أياماً كثيرة حصلت معاً ، بحسب تلك الدوائر المتوازية ، وذلك لا يقوله عاقل ، أو يقال : إنه ليس شيء منها نفس المدة والزمان ، بل المدة والزمان أمر مغاير لها ، مقدر لها بأسرها . وذلك هو المطلوب . ومما يقوى هذا الكلام : أن صريح العقل ناطق بأن حركات كل تلك الدوائر واقعة في زمان واحد ، فالعقل حكم بأن تلك الحركات بأسرها واقعة في زمان واحد ، وإن ذلك الزمان ظرف لها بأسرها ووعاء لها بأسرها ، وذلك يوجب القطع بأن الزمان مغاير للحركة .
The fourth proof: The greatest of the celestial spheres is the ecliptic. As for the spheres parallel to it, the closer they are to the ecliptic the faster their motion, and the farther they are from the ecliptic the slower their motion. So it appears that the daily motions occurring in the parallel spheres (which are parallel to the ecliptic) are many and vary in speed and slowness. If time were the motion of the sphere, then making it the motion of some of those spheres would be no more appropriate than making it the motions of the rest of the spheres. So either it is all of them, in which case it would follow that this one day would not be one day but many days occurring together, according to those parallel spheres—and no rational person would say that—or it is said that none of them is the duration and time itself, but rather the duration and time are something different from them, measuring them all. That is what is sought. And what strengthens this argument is that pure reason declares that the motions of all those spheres occur in one time. So reason judges that all those motions occur in one time, and that that time is a vessel for them all and a container for them all. That necessitates the certainty that time is distinct from motion.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a proof (al-hujja al-rabi'a) that time is not identical with motion. The argument proceeds by examining the celestial spheres. The greatest sphere is the ecliptic (al-mintaqa), and the spheres parallel to it move at different speeds depending on their distance from the ecliptic. The daily motions of these parallel spheres are many and vary in speed. If time were simply the motion of the sphere, then there would be no reason to single out one particular motion (e.g., the motion of the ecliptic) as the definition of time; any of these motions would equally be time. This leads to a dilemma: either time is the totality of all these motions, which would mean that a single day becomes many simultaneous days (since each sphere has its own motion), which is absurd; or time is none of these motions but something else that measures them all. The latter is the required conclusion. The passage then adds a strengthening remark: reason perceives that all these varied motions occur in one and the same time, so time must be a container or vessel for them all, distinct from any particular motion. This proves that time is different from motion.

الفلك
المنطقة
الدوائر المتوازية
المدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is just the measurement of motion, so it is essentially the same as motion.
Correction: This argument shows that multiple motions occur in one time, so time must be a common container distinct from any single motion.

Checkpoint

A) Time would be the slowest motion.
B) A single day would become many days occurring simultaneously.
C) Time would be undefined.
D) Motion would cease to exist.

Key Takeaway
Time is a single container that holds all motions, not a motion itself.

?
When you feel your life is moving too fast or too slow, do you forget that time itself is a constant vessel from Allah, unmoved by your rush? Are you living as if time is your own measured motion, rather than a gift that contains all your actions and will one day end?
?
The proof shows that reason itself demands that time be distinct from motion. Does your heart submit to that rational truth, or do you live as though your own motion defines time? What would it mean to let that truth shape how you use the time Allah has given you?

The Fifth Proof: Time Is Not Described as Fast or Slow
Sanusi presents the fifth proof for time-motion distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the fifth proof argues that time must be distinct from motion based on the properties of speed and slowness.

Core Idea
If time were motion, it would be fast or slow; but it is not.

This lesson presents the fifth proof for distinguishing time from motion. The argument is straightforward: motion can be described as fast or slow, but time itself never is. Moreover, our very concepts of speed and slowness are defined using time, showing that time is the measure, not the motion being measured. Let's examine how this reasoning establishes the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof in Arabic
Start by reading the Arabic passage aloud or silently. Notice the structure: it presents two sub-arguments linked by 'wa-ayḍan' (also).
The proof is concise; every word counts.
2
Identify the first argument
The first part states that motion is described as fast or slow, but time is not. Ask yourself: Can you think of an instance where time is called fast or slow? This shows a fundamental difference.
3
Understand the second argument
The second part explains that speed and slowness are understood only through time. A slower motion covers less distance in the same time or the same distance in more time. This shows time is the standard, not the motion itself.
This reinforces that time and motion are not identical.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Combine both arguments to see why they conclude that time is not motion. Write the conclusion in your own words.
The proof is logical; it does not rely on empirical observation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : إن الحركة توصف بالسرعة والبطء ، والزمان لا يوصف بذلك ، فإنه لا يقال : هذا الزمان أبطأ من ذلك الزمان ولا أسرع منه . وأيضاً : فإن سرعة الحركة وبطأها إنما يعقلان بسبب المدة والزمان ، فإنه يقال : الأبطأ هو الذي يقطع مثل ما قطعه السريع في زمان أطول ، أو يقطع أقل مما قطعه السريع في مثل زمان السريع ، والأسرع ما يكون بالضد منه ، وكل ذلك يدل على أن الزمان غير الحركة
The fifth proof: Motion is described as fast and slow, but time is not described as such, for it is not said 'this time is slower than that time' or 'faster than it'. Also, the speed and slowness of motion are only understood by means of duration and time, for it is said: the slower is that which covers the same distance as the faster in a longer time, or covers less than what the faster covers in the same time as the faster; and the faster is the opposite of that. All of this indicates that time is not motion.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a proof (al-hujja al-khamisa) for the distinction between time and motion. The argument is twofold. First, motion can be described as fast or slow, but time itself is never described as fast or slow—we don't say 'this time is faster than that time'. If time were identical with motion, then time would also be describable as fast or slow. Second, the concepts of speed and slowness are defined in terms of time: a slower motion covers the same distance in a longer time, or less distance in the same time. Thus time is the measure by which we judge speed, not the motion itself. Therefore, time is not motion.

Key Terms
السرعة
البطء
الزمان
الحركة
المدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that time could be fast or slow subjectively, but the argument shows that in philosophical terms, time itself has no speed.
Correction: The proof is based on objective description: we do not attribute speed to time itself, only to motions occurring in time.

Checkpoint
Why does the fifth proof conclude that time is not motion?
A) Because motion is eternal but time is not.
B) Because motion is described as fast or slow, but time is not.
C) Because time is a measure of motion.
D) Because motion requires time.

Key Takeaway
The fifth proof shows that because time cannot be called fast or slow, and because speed is defined relative to time, time must be distinct from motion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often say 'time flies' or 'time drags'. But this lesson says time itself is neither fast nor slow. How much of your anxiety about time is actually about your own motion through events, not time itself? What would change if you stopped blaming time and looked at your own movements?
?
If time is not motion, then your experience of time is not time itself. Are you measuring your life by events and speed, or by the steady measure that is time? What is one area where you could slow down and still use time well?
?
The proof shows that speed is defined by time. That means time is the standard by which you judge everything. Do you ever judge time itself as if it were moving? How does that misjudgment affect your relationship with Allah, who is the Creator of time?

The Sixth Proof: Time Is Not Motion
Sanusi presents the sixth proof that time is not motion using a thought experiment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth proof that time is distinct from motion, which uses a thought experiment of multiple independent spheres moving simultaneously.

Core Idea
A single time can contain many independent motions.

This lesson presents the sixth proof from Sanusi's argument that time is not the same as motion. Through a vivid thought experiment involving independent spheres in infinite void, the author demonstrates that we can conceive of many motions occurring together without conceiving of multiple times. This intuitive argument shows that time must be a single entity distinct from motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then its translation. Pay attention to the logical flow from supposition to conclusion.
The proof is concise; each sentence carries weight.
2
Visualize the thought experiment
Imagine many concentric spheres, each independent and moving. They are in infinite void and not connected. This is the starting point of the proof.
The spheres are not nested; they are separate.
3
Understand the intuitive knowledge
The proof claims we intuitively know that we cannot conceive of two separate times happening at the same moment. This is a key premise.
Badiha (intuition) is a source of knowledge in kalam.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since many independent motions exist together but cannot have multiple times, time cannot be identified with any single motion. Therefore time is distinct from motion.
This refutes the idea that time is motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : إنه يمكننا تعقل أفلاك كثيرة في الخلاء الذي لا نهاية له ، بحيث يكون كل واحد منها خارجاً عن الآخر ، وغير متعلق به . فعلى هذا التقدير يمكننا تصور حركات كثيرة معاً بحيث لا تكون منها تبعاً للأخرى. ونعلم بالبديهة : أنه لا يمكننا تعقل حصول زمانين ، فالحركة غير الزمان .
The sixth proof: We can conceive of many spheres in infinite void, such that each one is outside the other and not connected to it. According to this supposition, we can imagine many motions together, such that none of them is dependent on another. And we know intuitively that we cannot conceive of two times occurring. So motion is not time.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a proof (al-hujja al-sadisa) that time is not motion. It involves a thought experiment: we can imagine an infinite void containing many independent, non-concentric spheres that do not affect one another. We can suppose these spheres are all moving simultaneously. In that scenario, we have many independent motions occurring at the same time. Yet we cannot conceive of two separate times existing simultaneously. Therefore, these many motions must all occur in one and the same time. Since a single time can contain many independent motions, time cannot be identified with any one motion, nor with all of them collectively (as the fourth proof showed). Thus time must be distinct from motion. The argument relies on intuitive knowledge (badiha) that two times cannot occur simultaneously.

Key Terms
الزمان
الحركة
الخلاء
الأفلاك
البديهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that independent motions would each have their own time.
Correction: The proof shows we cannot conceive of two concurrent times, so all motions share one time.

Checkpoint
What does the sixth proof ask us to imagine?
A) Many moving spheres in infinite void.
B) A single sphere with variable speed.
C) The creation of time from motion.
D) The end of motion.

Key Takeaway
Time is not motion because a single time can accommodate many independent motions simultaneously.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You rely on time every moment, but this lesson shows that time is not merely your actions or movements. If each moment is a separate entity given by Allah, how many moments have you wasted without gratitude? Will you account for every second from now on?
?
The proof uses intuitive knowledge (badiha) that two times cannot coexist. What other truths about Allah and the unseen do you know intuitively but ignore in your daily life? Will you start acting on that inner certainty today?
?
Imagine the void with spheres moving independently, yet all share the same time. Your life may feel chaotic with many responsibilities, but time is one and limited. Are you using this single gift of time to seek Allah, or are you letting it slip away? Commit to one change in how you spend your hours.

Seventh Proof: Time is Not Motion (Distinctness Argument)
Seventh proof: motion occurs in time, not in motion or its attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seventh proof that time is distinct from motion and all its attributes, based on the impossibility of saying motion occurs in itself or in other motions.

Core Idea
Time is not motion because motion occurs in time, not in itself.

This lesson presents a concise proof from Al-Matalib al-Aliyah that time and motion are distinct. The argument focuses on how we describe motion's occurrence: we say it happens in a particular time, but we cannot say it happens in itself or in any of its attributes. This linguistic-conceptual point reveals that time is a separate container for motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the structure: the proof states what we can say (motion occurred in this time) and what we cannot say.
The passage is short but dense; pay attention to the word 'or' which lists alternatives.
2
Identify the four impossibilities
The passage lists four things motion cannot be said to occur in: itself, an attribute of itself, another motion, or an attribute of another motion. Jot these down.
These are the core of the proof.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Ask yourself: why does the impossibility of these alternatives prove that time is not motion? The answer is that time is the only valid container for motion, distinct from motion and its attributes.
This connects to the core idea of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : يمكننا أن نقول : هذه الحركة بجميع صفاتها ، حصلت في هذا الزمان ، ولم تحصل في الزمان المتقدم. ولا يمكننا أن نقول : حصلت هذه الحركة في نفسها ، أو في صفة من الصفات القائمة بها ، أو في حركة أخرى ، أو في صفة من الصفات القائمة بها ، وكل ذلك يدل على أن الزمان غير الحركة ، وغير جميع الصفات القائمة بالحركة
The seventh proof: We can say: this motion, with all its attributes, occurred in this time, and did not occur in the preceding time. But we cannot say: this motion occurred in itself, or in an attribute subsisting in it, or in another motion, or in an attribute of the attributes subsisting in it. All of this indicates that time is not motion, and is not any of the attributes subsisting in motion.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a proof (al-hujja al-sabi'a) that time is distinct from motion and from all attributes of motion. The argument is linguistic and conceptual: when we describe a motion, we say it occurred in a particular time (e.g., 'this motion happened yesterday'). We do not say it occurred in itself, nor in any of its own attributes (such as its speed or direction), nor in another motion, nor in any attribute of another motion. This shows that time is a separate entity that contains motion; it is not identical with motion or any of its qualities. Therefore, time is not motion.

Key Terms
الزمان
الحركة
الصفات
الحصول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People might think that saying 'motion occurred in time' is similar to saying 'it occurred in a place', but the argument shows that 'in' here is unique because motion cannot be located in itself.
Correction: The 'in' of time is not reducible to any intrinsic property of motion or to another motion; it indicates a distinct temporal dimension.

Checkpoint
According to the seventh proof, which of the following statements is impossible?
A) This motion occurred in this time.
B) This motion occurred in itself.
C) This motion occurred in the past.
D) This motion occurred slowly.

Key Takeaway
The seventh proof shows time is a distinct entity from motion because motion's temporal occurrence cannot be reduced to its own nature or to other motions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time is a separate container from your actions (motions), then every moment is a distinct gift from Allah, not something you create by moving. Do you live as if you can 'make time' or 'waste time', or do you recognize that each moment is given to you independently? What would change if you truly believed that time is a created entity that holds your deeds?
?
The proof shows that motion does not occur in its own attributes. This means your actions are not defined by their speed or quality (attributes) but by the time in which they occur. Are you more concerned with the 'attributes' of your deeds (how impressive they look) or with the time (the moment) in which they are done for Allah? How can you shift your focus to the present moment as the container of your worship?
?
Since time is not motion, your hurry and busyness do not create more time. Time is given; it does not depend on your movement. Are you constantly rushing as if you can stretch time by moving faster? How can you instead learn to receive each moment with calm awareness that it is a created gift from Allah, not a resource you produce?

Eighth Proof: Time Is Distinct from Motion
The eighth proof argues that we can conceive of time without any motion, e.g., after the annihilation of the cosmos.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the eighth proof that time is distinct from motion, and how a thought experiment about annihilation and recreation demonstrates time's independence.

Core Idea
Time can exist without motion—proving they are distinct.

The eighth proof in this discussion of time and motion uses a bold theological scenario: imagine that God destroys all bodies at the Resurrection, leaving only a stretch of absolute non-existence before He recreates everything. During that stretch, no motion occurs, yet we easily conceive of a duration. This thought experiment challenges the idea that time is merely a measure of motion. Let's examine the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Get a feel for the argument.
Notice the key terms: زمان, حركة, إعدام, إعادة.
2
Identify the supposition
The proof asks us to suppose that God annihilates the celestial sphere and all planets at the Resurrection, leaving everything in absolute non-existence for a period.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The proof points out that the duration between annihilation and recreation is a specific period, and the mind can imagine it being longer or shorter. During this period, there are no motions.
This shows that time is not dependent on motion.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Since we can conceive of time without motion, and this supposition is not intuitively impossible, time must be an independent reality distinct from motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة : إنه يمكننا أن نتصور زماناً خالياً عن الحركة . مثلاً : إذا توهمنا أن الله سبحانه أعدم الفلك ، وأعدم جميع الكواكب عند قيام القيامة ، ثم إنه تعالى ترك هذه الأشياء على العدم المحض مدة مديدة إلى أن يعيدها ، ويعيد الخلائق في موقف القيامة. فالمدة المتوسطة بين أول زمان الإعدام ، وأول زمان الإعادة لا شك أنها تكون مدة مخصوصة ، والعقل يمكنه فرض تلك المدة أقل ، أو أكثر ، أو أنقص ، أو أزيد ، ففي هذا الفرض قد فرضنا جميع الحركات معدومة ، وهذا الفرض ليس فرضاً معلوم الامتناع بالبديهة
The eighth proof: We can conceive of time devoid of motion. For example, if we suppose that God—exalted is He—annihilates the sphere and annihilates all the planets at the establishment of the Resurrection, and then He leaves these things in absolute non-existence for a long period until He brings them back and brings back the creatures at the standing of the Resurrection. Then the duration between the first moment of annihilation and the first moment of restoration is undoubtedly a specific duration, and the mind can suppose that duration to be less or more, shorter or longer. In this supposition, we have supposed all motions to be nonexistent, and this supposition is not a supposition known to be impossible intuitively.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a proof (al-hujja al-thamina) that time is independent of motion. It uses a theological thought experiment: imagine that God destroys the celestial sphere and all planets at the Resurrection, leaving everything in absolute nonexistence for a period. Then He later recreates them. During that intermediate period, there are no motions (since no bodies exist), yet we can conceive of a duration between the two events. The mind can even imagine varying that duration (longer or shorter). This shows that time can exist without motion, and therefore time is not identical with motion. The proof notes that this thought experiment is not obviously impossible; it is not a self-contradictory supposition. Thus time is an independent reality.

Key Terms

الحركة
الإعدام
الإعادة
العدم المحض
القيامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is merely a measure of motion and cannot exist without motion.
Correction: This proof shows that we can conceive of a duration when no motion occurs, meaning time is an independent reality.

Checkpoint

A) A time when all motions are faster.
B) A period of time with no motion at all.
C) The simultaneous occurrence of many motions.
D) The eternity of motion.

Key Takeaway
Time can be conceived independently of motion, so time is not the same as motion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
The proof says the mind can suppose a duration between annihilation and recreation. Do you truly believe that your Lord has control over every moment, even when nothing is moving? How can you cultivate a deeper trust in His power over time and your own life?

The Eleventh Argument: Duration Distinct from Motion
The author presents a logical proof for the distinction between duration and motion using the asymmetry of first/last suppositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical asymmetry between positing a first/last for motion vs. duration, and how this asymmetry proves that duration is a distinct reality from motion.

Core Idea
Duration's first moment forces a prior duration; motion's first moment does not—this difference proves they are distinct.

This lesson presents the eleventh argument from the author demonstrating that duration (al-mudda) is not the same as motion or any of its attributes. By comparing what happens when we posit a first or last moment for each, we uncover a fundamental logical difference that shows duration is a separate, underlying reality.

Guided Path
1
Understand the supposition for motion
Read the first part where the author considers positing a first moment of motion. Notice that it does not logically require a prior motion.
This is because motion can begin from a state of rest.
2
Understand the supposition for duration
Now read the part about positing a first moment of duration. Observe that it necessarily entails a prior duration.
The author argues that the priority of non-existence before the first moment can only be conceived through duration itself.
3
Compare the entailments
Contrast the two: motion's first does not imply prior motion, but duration's first implies prior duration. This asymmetry is key.
The same reasoning applies to positing a last for each.
4
Conclude the proof
Read the conclusion: because the logical implications differ, duration must be a reality distinct from motion and all its attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الحادية عشر: إنا إذا فرضنا أوّلاً للحركة ، فإنه لا يلزم من مجرد فرض أول للحركة ، حصول حركة قبل تلك الحركة ، لأنه لا يستبعد في العقل أن يكون الشيء ساكناً ثم يتحرك . وأيضاً : إذا فرضنا آخراً للحركة ، فإنه لا يلزمنا من مجرد هذا الفرض إثبات حركة بعد تلك الحركة ، لأنه لا يستبعد في العقل أن يكون الشيء متحركاً ، ثم يصير ساكناً . أما إذا فرضنا المدة أولاً ، لزمنا من مجرد هذا الفرض إثبات مدة قبل تلك المدة، لأن المدة لا يكون لها أول ، إلا إذا كان عدمها قبل وجودها وتلك القبلية لا يمكن حصولها ولا تعقلها ، إلا بسبب المدة . فثبت : أنا متى فرضنا للمدة ، فإنه يلزم من مجرد هذا الفرض كونها موجودة قبل ذلك ، وكذلك إذا فرضنا للمدة آخراً فإنه يلزم من مجرد فرض انقطاع المدة كونها موجودة بعد ذلك الانقطاع ، لأنه لا يحصل لها انقطاع ، إلا إذا حصل عدمها بعد وجودها ، وهذه البعدية لا يمكن تعقلها إلا عند حصول المدة ، فثبت : أن فرض أول وآخر للحركة ، لا يوجب إثبات حركة قبل ذلك وبعد ذلك الآخر ، وذلك يدل على أن المدة شيء مغاير للحركة ولجميع صفاتها وأحوالها
The eleventh argument: If we posit a first for motion, then merely from the supposition of a first for motion, it does not necessitate the occurrence of a motion before that motion, because it is not rationally improbable that a thing be at rest and then move. Also, if we posit a last for motion, then merely from this supposition it does not necessitate affirming a motion after that motion, because it is not rationally improbable that a thing be in motion and then become at rest. However, if we posit a first for duration (al-mudda), then merely from this supposition it would necessitate affirming a duration before that duration, because duration cannot have a first unless its non-existence precedes its existence, and that priority (al-qabliyya) cannot be attained nor conceived except by means of duration. So it is established that whenever we posit for duration, it follows from merely this supposition that it exists before that, and likewise if we posit a last for duration, then it follows from merely the supposition of the cessation of duration that it exists after that cessation, because it cannot have cessation unless its non-existence occurs after its existence, and this posteriority (al-ba'diyya) cannot be conceived except when duration exists. So it is established that positing a first and last for motion does not necessitate affirming a motion before that or after that last, and that indicates that duration is something distinct from motion and from all its attributes and states.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a proof (the eleventh argument) demonstrating that duration (al-mudda) is a reality distinct from motion and all its attributes. The author uses a logical comparison between positing a first or a last for motion and positing a first or a last for duration. For motion: if we suppose a first moment of motion, we do not logically have to posit a motion before it, because it is possible for something at rest to start moving. Similarly, if we suppose a last moment of motion, we do not have to posit a motion after it, because something moving can stop. For duration: if we suppose a first moment of duration, we are forced to posit a duration before that moment, because a first moment of duration means that non-existence preceded that moment, and that priority (qabliyya) can only be conceived through duration itself. Likewise, if we suppose a last moment of duration, we are forced to posit duration after that cessation, because the posteriority (ba'diyya) after cessation can only be conceived through duration. Thus, the logical entailments are different: positing a first or last for motion does not imply prior or subsequent motion, but for duration it does. This asymmetry proves that duration is not identical to motion or any of its properties; it is a distinct thing.

Key Terms
المدة (al-mudda)
الحركة (al-ḥaraka)
الأول (al-awwal)
الآخر (al-ākhir)
القبلية (al-qabliyya)
البعدية (al-ba'diyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time (duration) is merely the measure of motion and not a distinct reality.
Correction: This argument shows that time (duration) is logically prior and independent of motion, as the same suppositions yield different results.

Checkpoint
Why does positing a first for duration entail a prior duration, while positing a first for motion does not entail a prior motion?
A) Because motion can only exist with duration, so they are identical.
B) Because duration's first requires non-existence before it, and that priority is conceivable only through duration.
C) Because motion cannot have a last moment, while duration can.
D) Because the author assumes that duration is infinite and motion is finite.

Key Takeaway
Duration (al-mudda) is a reality distinct from motion, as shown by the logical asymmetry in their first/last suppositions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If duration is not merely the measure of motion but a distinct reality created by Allah, how does that change the way you view the time you have each day? Are you using that time as a sacred container for actions that please Him, or do you treat it as something that simply passes?
?
The argument shows that time has a dependent relationship with prior and posterior moments. In your spiritual life, do you feel that each moment is connected to the next in a way that demands accountability? How does this awareness affect your intentions (niyya) for the rest of today?
?
Consider that your life's duration will eventually have a last moment. The proof says that positing a last for duration implies a duration after it—ultimately, the eternal duration of the afterlife. Does this thought stir you to prepare for what comes after your last breath? What specific change can you make today to align your time with that reality?

Time as Self-Subsistent Substance
Author concludes time is self-subsistent and motion only measures it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author concludes that time is an independent substance and how he refutes the view that it is merely the measure of celestial motion.

Core Idea
Time exists by itself; celestial motion only measures it, not creates it.

This passage brings together the arguments from earlier proofs to reach a firm conclusion. The author asserts that time cannot be reduced to motion or its attributes. Instead, it is a self-subsistent reality. The analogy with clocks and sundials helps clarify that instruments only divide time, not bring it into existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the full translation. Let the author's conclusion come through.
Notice the emphatic phrasing 'فثبت بهذا' (so it is established).
2
Identify the negative and positive claims
The passage first negates two views: that time is the measure of motion, and that it is an attribute of motion. Then it positively establishes that duration is self-subsistent. Find each part.
The author uses 'فظهر' (so it appears) and 'فثبت' (so it is established).
3
Analyze the analogy
Reflect on how the example of sundials and clocks supports the conclusion. What do they have in common with celestial motion?
The point is that instruments measure but do not create.
4
Consider the final claim
The author ends by stating that for proponents, this knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī). Ask yourself: why would it be considered self-evident?
This connects to the broader discussion of epistemology in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فظهر بهذه البراهين القاهرة: أن الزمان والمدة لا يمكن أن يكون عبارة عن مقدار الحركة الفلكية ، وإذا بطل هذا بطل أيضاً : أن يكون الزمان عبارة عن صفة من صفات تلك الحركة ، وحالة من أحوالها . وبهذا يظهر فساد قول من يقول : إنه عبارة عن مقدار حركة فلك معدل النهار ، لأن مقدار تلك الحركة عبارة عن صفة من صفاتها ، وحالة من أحوالها وذلك مما أبطلناه . فثبت بهذا : أن المدة موجود قائم بنفسه مستقل بذاته، وأنه لا تأثير للحركة الفلكية في وجود المدة والزمان البتة ، وإنما تأثيرها في تقدير هذه المدة بالأجزاء والأبعاض. ومثاله : تقدير الليل والنهار بالفنجانات ، وصندوق الساعات ، فإن تلك الآلات لا تأثير لها في إيجاد الزمان والمدة ، وإنما تأثيرها في تقسيم الليل والنهار بالساعات والأجزاء ، فكذلك تأثير الحركة الفلكية ليس في تكوين المدة وإيجادها ، بل في تقسيمها بالأجزاء والأبعاض ، وهي : السنون والشهور والأيام والساعات . فهذا تقرير مذاهب هؤلاء الذين يقولون : العلم بوجود المدة وبكونها أمراً مغايراً للحركة الفلكية ، ولجميع أحوال هذه الحركة : علم ضروري.
So it appears by these conclusive proofs that time (al-zaman) and duration (al-mudda) cannot be the measure of celestial motion. And when this is invalidated, it is also invalidated that time be an attribute of those motions or a state of their states. And by this the corruption of the statement of those who say that it is the measure of the motion of the celestial equator becomes apparent, because the measure of that motion is an attribute of its attributes and a state of its states, and that is what we have invalidated. So it is established by this that duration is an existent subsisting by itself, independent in its essence, and that celestial motion has no effect in the existence of duration and time at all; rather, its effect is only in the measurement of this duration by parts and portions. An example of that is the measurement of night and day by sundials and the box of clocks, for those instruments have no effect in bringing about time and duration; rather, their effect is only in dividing night and day into hours and parts. Likewise, the effect of celestial motion is not in the formation of duration and its bringing-into-existence, but rather in its division into parts and portions, which are years, months, days, and hours. So this is the exposition of the schools of those who say: knowledge of the existence of duration and that it is something distinct from celestial motion and from all states of this motion is necessary (ḍarūrī) knowledge.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage draws the conclusion from the preceding proofs. First, it states that time (al-zaman) and duration (al-mudda) cannot be the measure of celestial motion, nor an attribute of that motion. Then it specifically refutes those who say time is the measure of the motion of the celestial equator (falak muʻaddil al-nahār), because that measure is also an attribute of motion, which has already been invalidated. The positive conclusion is that duration is an existent that subsists by itself (qāʼim bi-nafsihi) and is independent in its essence (mustaqill bi-dhātihi). Celestial motion has no effect on bringing time into existence; its only effect is in measuring duration into parts and portions. The author gives an analogy: instruments like sundials and clocks do not create night and day; they only divide them into hours. Similarly, celestial motion does not create time, but divides it into years, months, days, and hours. Finally, the author states that for those who hold this position, knowledge of the existence of duration and its distinction from celestial motion is necessary (ḍarūrī) knowledge—i.e., self-evident to the intellect.

Key Terms
الزمان (al-zaman)
المدة (al-mudda)
الحركة الفلكية (al-ḥaraka al-falakiyya)
فلك معدل النهار (falak muʻaddil al-nahār)
قائم بنفسه (qāʼim bi-nafsihi)
مستقل بذاته (mustaqill bi-dhātihi)
علم ضروري (ʿilm ḍarūrī)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Celestial motion brings time into existence.
Correction: The author argues that motion only measures and divides a pre-existing duration, it does not create it.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the effect of celestial motion on duration?
A) It brings duration into existence.
B) It measures and divides duration into parts.
C) It gives duration its essential nature.
D) It has no effect whatsoever.

Key Takeaway
Time is a self-subsistent reality, not created or measured by motion; motion only divides it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time is self-subsistent and not caused by anything, then your existence in time is not something created by the cycles of day and night. How then should you regard the passing of each moment as a gift from the One who sustains time itself, and what will you do with the time you have right now?
?
The author says knowledge that time is distinct from motion is ‘necessary’ (ḍarūrī). Yet many people live as if time only has meaning through their busy schedules and the movements of the sun. Examine your own life: Do you treat time as an independent reality that you must steward, or do you act as if your own activities create time? What would change if you truly believed time exists before your next appointment?
?
Celestial motion only measures time—it does not create it. That means the sun, moon, and stars are signs, not sources, of time. Are you more attached to the measurement (the clock, the calendar) than to the reality of time that points you to the Eternal? How can you realign your heart today to see time as a created measure that points to its Creator?
