The First Hypothesis: Imkan’s Fixed Measure
First hypothesis: a single fast motion shows imkan's fixed measure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the first motion scenario demonstrates that imkan (possibility) has a fixed particularity and is not a mere logical abstraction.

Core Idea
Imkan is not arbitrary; it has a specific measure that cannot be altered with the same speed.

The author begins by considering a fast motion that covers a specific distance at a specific speed. He argues that the possibility (imkan) associated with this motion has a fixed measure: it cannot be increased or decreased while preserving the same speed. This suggests that imkan is a real attribute with its own particularity, distinct from the motion itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the first hypothesis
Carefully read the Arabic passage describing the fast motion and the claim about its possibility. Pay attention to the language of ‘increase’ and ‘decrease’.
The passage uses ‘لا يمكن أن يزاد’ and ‘لا أن ينقص’.
2
Identify the key claim
The author states that this possibility has a ‘particularity in itself’ (خصوصية في نفسه). What does that imply?
It implies a real attribute, not a mere concept.
3
Reflect on the reasoning
Why does the impossibility of increase or decrease while keeping speed constant indicate a fixed measure? Consider how this sets the stage for proving imkan is quantitative.
4
Connect to the overall goal
Understand that this hypothesis is the first of three that together prove imkan is a distinct quantitative attribute.
This lesson focuses only on the first hypothesis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بين أخذ هذا السريع وتركه ، إمكان قطع مثل هذه المسافة بمثل هذه السرعة ، وأن في مثل هذا القدر من الإمكان ، وبمثل هذه السرعة ، لا يمكن أن يزاد على هذه المسافة ، ولا أن ينقص منها ، فهذا الإمكان له في نفسه خصوصية ، ولا يقبل حركة بهذا القدر من السرعة ، إلا في مثل هذا القدر من المسافة (١) ، ولا يقبل الأزيد منها ، [ ولا بمثلي الأقل منها (۳) ] ، فهذا الإمكان له في حد ذاته خصوصية وحقيقة، باعتبارها حصل له هذا الامتياز والاختصاص . وأما الفرض الثاني وهو [ وجود (۳) ] حركتين متساويتين في السرعة والبطء ، مختلفتين في الأخذ ، متساويتين في الترك، فههنا السريع الثاني (1) يقطع من المسافة ، أقل وغرضنا منه أمران : الأول : إن الإمكان الذي يحصل فيه هذا السريع الثاني ، جزء من الإمكان الذي يحصل فيه السريع الأول ، فيكون هذا الإمكان قابلا للتطبيق وللزيادة والنقصان ، فوجب كونه موجوداً قابلاً للمساواة والمفاوتة . والثاني : إن هذا السريع الأصغر مشارك للسريع الأكبر في كونه حركة ، وفي كونها سريعة ، وفي مقدار المتحرك. وخالفها في مقدار هذا الإمكان . وما به المشاركة غير ما به المباينة، فيثبت أن هذا الإمكان يجب أن يكون أمراً مغايراً لنفس ماهية الحركة، ومغايراً لبطء الحركة ولسرعتها ، ومغايراً لمقدار جوهر المتحرك . وأما الفرض الثالث وهو وجود حركتين مختلفتين في السرعة والبطء ، متساويتين في الأخذ والترك . فاعلم : أن غرضنا من هذا الفرض : بيان أن هذا الإمكان مغاير لمقدار المتحرك، ولمقدار المسافة ، وذلك لأنه ظهر بهذا الفرض أن البطىء والسريع، إن اشتركا في مقدار المسافة ، اختلفا في مقدار هذا الإمكان. وإن اشتركا في مقدار هذا الإمكان اختلفا في مقدار المسافة ، وذلك يوجب القطع بأن مقدار هذا الإمكان أمر مغاير لمقدار المسافة . فثبت أن هذه الأمور الثلاثة من الفرض ، ظهر أن هذا الإمكان [ أمر (۱) ] موجود مقداري ، وأنه مغاير لنفس مقدار المتحرك ، ولنفس مقدار المسافة ، ولنفس ولكون الحركة سريعة أو بطيئة . وذلك هو المقصود . وهذا تقرير تمام هذه الحجة .
Between the taking of this fast motion and its leaving, the possibility (al-imkan) of covering such a distance with such a speed, and that in this measure of possibility, and with this speed, it cannot be increased beyond this distance nor decreased from it. So this possibility has a particularity in itself, and it does not accept a motion with this measure of speed except in this measure of distance, and it does not accept more than it, nor less than half of it. So this possibility has in itself a particularity and a reality by which it acquires this distinction and specification. As for the second hypothesis, which is the existence of two motions equal in speed and slowness, differing in taking, equal in leaving: here the second fast motion covers less of the distance. Our purpose from it is two things: First: that the possibility in which this second fast motion occurs is a part of the possibility in which the first fast motion occurs, so this possibility is divisible and subject to increase and decrease, so it must be an existing thing capable of equality and inequality. Second: that this smaller fast motion shares with the larger fast motion in that it is a motion, in that it is fast, and in the measure of the moving body, but differs from it in the measure of this possibility. That by which they participate is other than that by which they differ, so it is established that this possibility must be something distinct from the very essence of motion, distinct from the slowness and speed of the motion, and distinct from the measure of the substance of the moving body. As for the third hypothesis, which is the existence of two motions differing in speed and slowness, equal in taking and leaving: know that our purpose from this hypothesis is to show that this possibility is distinct from the measure of the moving body and from the measure of the distance. That is because it appears from this hypothesis that the slow and the fast, if they share in the measure of distance, differ in the measure of this possibility; and if they share in the measure of this possibility, they differ in the measure of the distance. That necessitates the conclusion that the measure of this possibility is distinct from the measure of the distance. So it is established from these three hypotheticals that this possibility is an existing quantitative thing, distinct from the very measure of the moving body, from the very measure of the distance, and from the very fact of the motion being fast or slow. That is the intended goal. This is the complete exposition of this argument.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage presents a philosophical proof that the possibility (al-imkan) inherent in a motion is not a mere logical relation but a real quantitative attribute distinct from the motion itself, its speed, slowness, the moving body, and the distance covered. The author uses three hypothetical scenarios about motions to argue this point. First hypothetical: a fast motion covers a specific distance in a given time with a certain possibility measure; this possibility cannot be increased or decreased while preserving the same speed, indicating it has a fixed particularity. Second hypothetical: two motions equal in speed and slowness but one starts later and stops at the same time. The later one covers less distance, so its possibility is a part of the first's possibility, showing possibility is divisible and quantitative. Moreover, the two motions share being motion and speed but differ in possibility measure, proving possibility is distinct from motion and speed. Third hypothetical: two motions differing in speed but covering the same distance in the same time; here, if they share distance, they differ in possibility; if they share possibility, they differ in distance, proving possibility is distinct from distance as well. Thus, the three cases establish that possibility is an existing quantitative attribute separate from motion, speed, slowness, moving body, and distance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that possibility (imkan) is just a mental concept with no real measure.
Correction: The first hypothesis shows that imkan has a fixed measure that cannot be altered given constant speed, indicating it is a real attribute with quantitative particularity.

Checkpoint
What does the first hypothesis demonstrate about the possibility (al-imkan) of a fast motion?
A) It can be increased or decreased freely.
B) It has a fixed measure that cannot be increased or decreased with the same speed.
C) It is identical to the speed of motion.
D) It depends on the starting point of the motion.

Key Takeaway
The first hypothesis establishes that imkan has a fixed particularity, meaning it is a real attribute with a definite measure, not a mere abstraction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that what is possible for you is limited only by your own effort? This passage shows that possibility itself has fixed measures. How does that change how you view your own capabilities and reliance on Allah?
?
If imkan has a specific measure, then each action you take has a real possibility that Allah has set. Are you living with the awareness that your abilities are precisely measured? Or do you take them for granted?
?
The passage argues that possibility cannot be increased or decreased. Are you dissatisfied with the possibilities Allah has placed before you? What does this passage teach you about accepting Allah's precise decree?

The Second Hypothesis: Imkan is Divisible and Distinct from Motion
Second hypothesis: two motions equal in speed, differing in start time, show imkan is divisible and distinct.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two motions equal in speed but different in start time prove that imkan is divisible and distinct from motion itself.

Core Idea
Imkan is divisible and distinct from motion, speed, and the moving body.

The second hypothetical considers two motions with the same speed but starting at different times and ending at the same moment. The later motion covers less distance, so its possibility is part of the earlier motion's possibility. This shows that possibility can be divided and measured, and it is distinct from the motion's essence, speed, and the moving body.

Guided Path
1
Read the second hypothesis
Read the Arabic passage describing two motions equal in speed but differing in start time. Note the key terms: 'مختلفتين في الأخذ' (differing in taking) and 'متساويتين في الترك' (equal in leaving).
2
Identify the two purposes
The author states two purposes: first, to show divisibility (the later motion's possibility is part of the earlier's); second, to show distinction from motion and speed.
3
Analyze the shared and differing aspects
The motions share being motion, speed, and moving body, but differ in possibility measure. What does that imply about possibility?
If they share some attributes but differ in possibility, then possibility is not the same as those shared attributes.
4
Conclude the distinctness of imkan
The passage concludes that possibility must be distinct from the essence of motion, speed, slowness, and the moving body's magnitude.
This is a key step in proving imkan as a separate quantitative attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have possibilities in your life—abilities, time, opportunities. This lesson argues that possibility is a real, quantitative thing that can increase or decrease. When you look at your own potential, do you treat it as something fixed or as something that can expand? Are you actively measuring and growing your possibilities, or are you assuming they are what they are? What specific action will you take today to increase one of your possibilities?
?
The lesson shows that two people with the same speed and body can have different possibilities due to different start times. Think of a failure or missed opportunity you blame on your abilities. Could it be that your start time or circumstances, not your capability, limited your possibility? How does that change the way you view your past—and the way you plan your future? Commit to adjusting your strategy for one goal based on this insight.
?
Possibility here is distinct from motion itself. Have you ever confused your activity (motion) with your genuine potential? For example, busyness does not equal effectiveness. Are you measuring your worth by how much you move, or by the real possibility you are actualizing? Identify one area where you are busy but not actualizing your potential. What will you stop or start doing to align your motion with your possibility?

The Third Hypothesis: Imkan is Distinct from Distance and the Overall Conclusion
Third hypothesis and overall conclusion: imkan distinct from distance and the final summary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the third hypothesis proves imkan is distinct from distance, and how all three hypotheses collectively establish imkan as a real quantitative attribute.

Core Idea
Imkan is distinct from distance, and together the three hypotheses confirm imkan is an existing quantitative entity.

The third hypothetical considers two motions differing in speed but covering the same distance in the same time. By comparing their possibilities, the author shows that imkan is not the same as distance. He then concludes that all three hypotheses collectively prove imkan is an existing quantitative thing distinct from motion, speed, moving body, and distance.

Guided Path
1
Read the third hypothesis and conclusion
Read the Arabic passage describing two motions of different speeds but same distance and time. Follow the argument about sharing and differing.
2
Understand the argument of mutual exclusivity
The author argues: if the motions share distance, they differ in possibility; if they share possibility, they differ in distance. This shows possibility is not the same as distance.
This is a classic argument for distinctness.
3
Examine the concluding synthesis
The final sentences summarize that all three hypotheses together prove imkan is an existing quantitative thing, distinct from moving body, distance, and the quality of being fast or slow.
This is the culmination of the entire argument.
4
Reflect on the overall proof
Consider how each hypothesis covered a different aspect: fixed measure, divisibility/distinctness from motion, and distinctness from distance. Together they build a comprehensive case.

D) That it is not a real attribute.

Key Takeaway
The third hypothesis and the conclusion together confirm that imkan is a real quantitative attribute distinct from distance, moving body, and motion's speed.

The author uses careful logic to separate outward circumstances (distance, speed) from inner reality (imkan). In what area of your life have you confused your external conditions with your true potential? Commit to one specific step to realign your focus.

First Objection: Argument Presupposes Time
The objector argues that the three hypotheticals presuppose the existence of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objector claims that the argument for the existence of time depends on premises that themselves presuppose time, making it circular or incomplete.

Core Idea
The objection argues that the proof's own premises need time, so it cannot prove time without circularity.

This passage presents the first objection against a previous argument. The objector identifies three hypotheticals used in the argument: fast motion, simultaneous motion, and sequential motion. Each of these, when examined, requires the concept of time. Since the argument was meant to demonstrate time's existence, this is a serious challenge. The passage ends with the beginning of the reply, setting up the next discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: the objection states the three hypotheticals and then shows each depends on time.
2

The passage lists three matters: 1) fast and slow motion, 2) two motions beginning and ending together, 3) one motion after another. List them.
3
Understand why each requires time
For each hypothetical, the objector explains that the concept involved (speed, instant, priority) cannot be defined without time. Work through each explanation.
4
Appreciate the objection's force
The objection is that the argument's premises are not foundational; they presuppose time. This means the argument cannot be used to prove time without circularity.
The full answer to this objection comes later.

Proof of a Distinct Magnitude of Possibility
Conclusion of a proof that possibility is a distinct quantitative existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a supposition about slow and fast motions demonstrates that the magnitude of possibility is a real quantitative entity distinct from distance, motion, and the moving object.

Core Idea
The magnitude of possibility is a real quantity, proven distinct from distance and motion.

This passage concludes a key proof in Islamic physics and metaphysics: that 'possibility' (al-imkan) is not just a mental concept but a real, measurable quantity. By comparing slow and fast motions, the author shows that the measure of possibility must be distinct from the measure of distance. This distinction is crucial for understanding the nature of time, motion, and change.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully, then the English translation. Notice how the argument uses a conditional: if they share distance, they differ in possibility; if they share possibility, they differ in distance.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the three things mentioned: moving object, distance, motion speed. Understand that the argument shows possibility is distinct from all three.
3
Grasp the logical structure
The argument is a two-way implication (if...then) that forces a distinction. Follow the logic: sharing one measure implies differing in the other, so the two measures cannot be identical.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that possibility has a quantitative existence separate from the object, distance, and quality of motion. This is the intended point.
This refutes the idea that possibility is merely mental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرض أن البطىء والسريع، إن اشتركا في مقدار المسافة ، اختلفا في مقدار هذا الإمكان. وإن اشتركا في مقدار هذا الإمكان اختلفا في مقدار المسافة ، وذلك يوجب القطع بأن مقدار هذا الإمكان أمر مغاير لمقدار المسافة . فثبت أن هذه الأمور الثلاثة من الفرض ، ظهر أن هذا الإمكان أمر موجود مقداري ، وأنه مغاير لنفس مقدار المتحرك ، ولنفس مقدار المسافة ، ولنفس ولكون الحركة سريعة أو بطيئة . وذلك هو المقصود . وهذا تقرير تمام هذه الحجة .
The supposition is that the slow and the fast, if they share in the measure of distance, they differ in the measure of this possibility. And if they share in the measure of this possibility, they differ in the measure of distance, and that necessitates the certainty that the measure of this possibility is something distinct from the measure of distance. So it is established that these three things [are] from supposition; it appears that this possibility is an existing quantitative [thing], and that it is distinct from the measure of the moving object itself, and from the measure of distance itself, and from the motion being fast or slow. And that is the intended [conclusion]. And this is the complete elaboration of this proof.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage concludes a proof establishing that the magnitude of possibility (al-imkan) is a real, quantitative entity distinct from the magnitude of the moving object, the magnitude of distance, and the quality of motion (fast or slow). The argument is based on a supposition: if a slow and a fast motion cover the same distance, they differ in the measure of possibility; if they share the measure of possibility, they differ in the measure of distance. This necessitates that the measure of possibility is distinct from the measure of distance. Thus the three things (the object, distance, and motion) are hypothetical; it becomes clear that possibility has a quantitative existence of its own. The author then declares that this is the intended conclusion and that this completes the proof.

Correction: The proof demonstrates that possibility has a quantitative existence distinct from distance, motion, and the object—it is a real magnitude in the world.

First Objection: Circularity in Proving Time's Existence
An objection that the proof assumes time, leading to circularity, and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection against the proof of time's existence—that it is circular—and the subsequent response and refutation.

Core Idea
A proof that assumes what it tries to prove is logically invalid.

The first objection targets the logical structure of the proof for time's existence. The objector argues that each premise of the proof already presupposes the existence of time, making the argument circular. We will examine the objection, a potential response, and the final refutation, which shows that the response fails to break the circularity.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning until the conditional statement. Notice how the objector lists three premises.
2
Analyze the three premises
For each premise, understand why the objector claims it requires prior knowledge of time. The first premise about fast and slow motions involves comparison over times.
3
Examine the conditional
The objector presents two possibilities: time's existence is either self-evident or needs proof. If self-evident, the proof is unnecessary; if not, the proof is circular because premises cannot be established without time.
4
Study the response and refutation
A hypothetical responder says that only the essence of time is intuitive, while its detailed nature is proven. The refutation shows that the proof does not actually provide details; it only shows existence, so circularity persists.
The refutation uses the distinction between existence and essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاعتراض عليها من وجوه : السؤال الأول : إنكم بنيتم هذه الحجة على أمور ثلاثة : فأحدها: أن ههنا حركة سريعة وحركة بطيئة . وثانيها : أن ههنا حركتين يبتدئان معاً ، وينقطعان معاً . وثالثها : أن ههنا حركتين تبتدىء إحداهما بعد الأخرى . ومن المعلوم : أن هذه الأمور الثلاثة لا يمكن اعتقاد حصولها إلا بعد الجزم بوجود الزمان . أما الأول : فلأن السريع هو الذي يقطع مثل ما قطعه البطيء في زمان أقل أو أزيد مما قطعه البطيء في زمان مساو، وأما البطيء فبالعكس من هذا الذي قلناه . ومعلوم : أن هذه الأحوال لا يتقرر ثبوتها إلا بعد تسليم وجود الزمان . وأما الثاني : وهو قولنا : في الحركتين إنهما يبتدئان معاً، وينتهيان معاً، فمعناه : أن ابتداء وجودهما، وانتهاء وجودهما يكون في آن واحد، لكن الآن لا يعقل، ولا يوجد إلا بعد تعقل الزمان . وأما الثالث : وهو أن تبتدىء إحدى الحركتين بعد الأخرى، فمعلوم أنه لا يمكن تصور معنى القبلية والبعدية، إلا بعد وجود الزمان . إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : وجود الزمان إما أن يكون غنياً عن الاستدلال، أو محتاجاً إلى الاستدلال. فإن كان الأول كان الخوض في هذا الدليل غنياً عنه، وإن كان الثاني فنقول : إنكم إنما بينتم وجود الزمان بهذه المقدمات وقد بينا أنه لا يمكن إثبات هذه المقدمات إلا بعد العلم بوجود الزمان، فيلزم الدور، ومعلوم أنه باطل . لا يقال : وجود أصل الزمان معلوم بالبديهة، فأما بيان ماهيته على التفصيل فذاك معلوم بالاستدلال، ونحن إنما أثبتنا بهذا الدليل تفصيل ماهيته، وحينئذ يسقط الدور. لأنا نقول : إن هذا القدر الذي سبق ذكره من الاستدلال، لا يدل على بيان ماهيته المعينة وحقيقته المخصوصة، بل لا دلالة فيه إلا على كونه أمراً موجوداً في الأعيان، وحينئذ يعود الدور المذكور .
And the objections to it are from aspects: The first question: You have built this proof on three things: First, that there is a fast motion and a slow motion. Second, that there are two motions that begin together and terminate together. Third, that there are two motions one of which begins after the other. And it is known that these three things cannot be believed to occur except after being certain of the existence of time. As for the first: because the fast is that which covers like what the slow covered in less time or more than what the slow covered in equal time, and as for the slow, it is the opposite of what we said. And it is known that these states are not established except after admitting the existence of time. As for the second: which is our saying concerning the two motions, that they begin together and end together; its meaning is that the beginning of their existence and the ending of their existence occur in one instant, but the instant is not conceivable nor does it exist except after conceiving time. As for the third: which is that one of the two motions begins after the other, it is known that the meaning of priority and posteriority cannot be conceived except after the existence of time. If you have understood this, we say: The existence of time is either independent of inference or needful of inference. If it is the first, then engaging in this proof is unnecessary; if it is the second, we say: You have only established the existence of time by these premises, and we have shown that these premises cannot be established except after knowing the existence of time, so circularity follows, and it is known that it is false. It cannot be said: The existence of the essence of time is known by intuition, but detailed explanation of its essence is known by inference, and we have only proven by this proof the detailed explanation of its essence, and then the circularity is removed. [But] we say: This amount of inference that was mentioned does not indicate the detailed explanation of its specific essence and its particular reality, rather it only indicates that it is an existent thing in external reality, and then the mentioned circularity returns.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection to the previous proof and its answer. The objector argues that the proof's three premises (the existence of fast/slow motions, two motions beginning/ending together, and two motions sequential) all presuppose the existence of time. Therefore, the proof is circular if it claims to prove time's existence. The objector then considers two possibilities: either time's existence is self-evident (making the proof unnecessary) or it needs proof (but then the premises cannot be established without time, causing circularity). The answer (raised by 'لا يقال' and answered by 'لأنا نقول') responds that the objector might claim that only the existence of time's essence is obvious by intuition, while its detailed nature is proven by this argument. The refutation (لأنا نقول) states that the proof does not actually demonstrate the specific essence; it only shows that time is an existent thing in external reality, so the circularity still stands. Thus the objection is deemed valid, and the proof is problematic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any proof that uses time as a premise is automatically circular.
Correction: The circularity only occurs if the premises cannot be known without already knowing the conclusion. In this objection, the objector shows that the premises do require prior knowledge of time.

Checkpoint
According to the first objection, why does the proof lead to circularity?
A) Because it uses premises that themselves require time to be known.
B) Because it assumes time is self-evident.
C) Because it defines time incorrectly.
D) Because it uses false premises about motion.

Key Takeaway
The first objection successfully demonstrates that the proof for time's existence is circular because it relies on premises that cannot be established without assuming time, and the response that the proof only clarifies time's essence fails.

Second Objection: Time's Lacking Existence as a Continuous Entity
An objection that time cannot be judged to have increase/decrease because its parts do not persist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection to the proof for time's existence, which argues that because time's parts do not persist, it cannot be judged to have increase or decrease in external reality, and thus the proof commits a fallacy.

Core Idea
Time's lack of persistent parts makes it impossible to judge as increasing or decreasing in the real world.

This passage presents a sophisticated objection to a kalām proof for time's existence. The objector points out that if a thing must actually exist to be judged as having increase or decrease, then time—whose parts are transitory—cannot be so judged in reality. Only a mental depiction can be, and that does not prove time's external reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: premise, application, distinction, conclusion.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the key premise
Find the premise that 'that which is judged to have increase and decrease must be existent.' This is from the opponent's doctrine.
This premise was used earlier to answer another argument.
3
Apply the premise to time
The objector says time is a perishing thing whose parts have no permanence. Therefore, it cannot truly be judged to have increase or decrease in reality.
4
Distinguish real vs. imaginary
Notice the distinction: the continuous entity depicted in the imagination can be judged as increasing/decreasing, but time itself has no external existence as a continuum.
This is the crux of the objection.
5
Understand the conclusion
The objector concludes that the proof is a sophism because it confuses a mental construct with real existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسؤال الثاني على هذا الدليل : إن من مذهبكم أن المحكوم عليه بالزيادة والنقصان ، لا بد وأن يكون موجوداً . وبه أجبتم عن دليل من استدل على أن للحركات أولاً بسبب كونها قابلة للزيادة والنقصان ، ثم إن من المعلوم من الأمور المنقضية، التي لا ثبات لأجزائها، ولا استقرار لأقسامها، وإذا كان كذلك، فحينئذ لا يصح الحكم عليه بالزيادة والنقصان في نفس الأمر . بل غاية ما في الباب : أن الأمر الممتد المرتسم منه في الوهم ، يمكن الحكم عليه بالزيادة والنقصان ، وأما الأمر الممتد من الزمان ، فلا وجود له البتة في الأعيان. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : الأمر الذي تريدون إثباته وهو وجود الزمان في الأعيان فإنه لا يمكن الحكم عليه بكونه قابلا للزيادة والنقصان . والذي صدق عليه هذا الحكم، وهو الأمر المفروض في الذهن فإنه لا يدل على كون الزمان موجوداً في الأعيان . فثبت أن هذه الحجة مغالطة .
And the second question against this proof: [It is] that [according to] your doctrine, that which is judged to have increase and decrease must be existent. And by this you answered the argument of one who argued that motions have a beginning because they are susceptible to increase and decrease. Then it is known that [time is] among perishing things, whose parts have no permanence and whose divisions have no stability. If that is the case, then it is not valid to judge it to have increase and decrease in reality. Rather, the utmost in this matter is that the extended thing depicted from it in the imagination can be judged to have increase and decrease. As for the extended thing of time, it has no existence whatsoever in external realities. If this is established, we say: The thing that you want to prove, which is the existence of time in external realities, cannot be judged to be susceptible to increase and decrease. And that which this judgment is true of, which is the thing supposed in the mind, does not indicate that time exists in external realities. So it is established that this argument is a sophism.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents a second objection to the proof. It begins by noting a premise from the opponent's own doctrine: that anything judged to have increase or decrease must actually exist. The opponent used this premise to refute someone who argued that motions have a beginning because they admit increase/decrease. The objector then points out that time is a perishing thing; its parts do not persist. Therefore, time cannot be truly judged to have increase or decrease in external reality. At most, the continuous entity depicted in the imagination can be judged that way, but time itself does not exist as an external continuum. Hence, the thing the proof aims to establish—time's real existence—cannot be shown to admit increase/decrease, while the imaginary entity that does admit it does not prove time's external existence. Thus, the proof is a fallacy (مغالطة).

Key Terms
الزيادة والنقصان
الوجود في الأعيان
الوهم
المغالطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because we can mentally conceive of time as a continuous thing that increases/decreases, time must actually exist as such in external reality.
Correction: This objection distinguishes between the mental depiction (which can be judged) and real time (which lacks persistent parts and does not exist as an external continuum). The proof fails because it confuses the two.

Checkpoint
According to the second objection, why is the proof a sophism (مغالطة)?
A) Because time is not real at all.
B) Because the predicate of increase/decrease applies only to an imaginary extension, not to time itself.
C) Because the opponent's doctrine is false.
D) Because the proof uses premises that are not known.

Key Takeaway
The second objection shows that the predicate 'increase/decrease' cannot apply to time in external reality, so the proof that time exists is based on a fallacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan your day, do you treat time as a container that exists independently, or do you realize it is merely a succession of moments created by Allah? How might this realization change your sense of urgency and reliance on Allah?
?
This objection shows that our mind can imagine a continuous 'thing' that has no external reality. What other concepts in your life might be mere imaginations that you treat as real? Examine one such assumption and ask yourself: does it have true existence in Allah's sight, or is it a mental construct?
?
If time is not a persisting entity, then your 'past' and 'future' are not real places. Does this change how you think about regret or anxiety? Will you commit to living in the present moment of Allah's decree?

First Proof: Priority as Attribute of Non-Existence
First proof that priority is an attribute of non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why priority cannot be an existent attribute based on the argument that it is an attribute of non-existence.

Core Idea
Priority is an attribute of non-existence, so it cannot be an existent attribute.

The first proof begins with a simple observation from plain reason: every originated thing is preceded by its non-existence. This suggests that priority itself is a quality of non-existence rather than a real attribute. Let's see how the author establishes this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author states the premise and conclusion.
The passage is short and direct.
2
Understand the reasoning
Identify the key claim: priority is an attribute of non-existence. Consider why an existent attribute cannot subsist in non-existence.
3
See the conclusion
The conclusion is that priority and posteriority are not among existent attributes. Reflect on the simplicity of this argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : الذي يدل على أن القبلية والبعدية لا يمكن أن يكونا من الأمور الموجودة : وجوه : الأول : إن صريح العقل يحكم بأن كل محدث ، فإنه مسبوق بعدمه ، وأن عدمه سابق على وجوده. وهذا يقتضي كون القبلية والسبق والتقدم وصفاً للعدم ، وما كان وصفاً للعدم ، امتنع أن يكون صفة موجودة ، لامتناع قيام الصفة الموجودة بالمعدوم المحض والنفي الصرف. فثبت : أن القبلية والبعدية ليست من الصفات الموجودة . الثاني : لو كانت القبلية صفة موجودة ، لكانت تلك الصفة الموجودة بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، إما أن تكون قبلاً أو معاً أو بعداً ، ويلزم التسلسل . لا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن تكون القبلية بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، وإن كانت قبلاً ، إلا أن كونها كذلك عين ذاته. لا أنه صفة زائدة على الذات ؟ لأنا نقول : إذا حكمنا على القبلية بأنها قبل شيء آخر ، فههنا ذات القبلية هي الموضوع . ثم حكمنا عليها بأنها قبل شيء آخر هو المحمول ، ومحمول القضية غير موضوعها لا محالة . فثبت : أن القبلية لو كانت صفة موجودة لكان كونها قبلاً بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، يمتنع أن يكون عين ذاتها ، بل لا بد وأن يكون أمراً مغايراً لذاتها . الثالث : إن القبلية والبعدية إضافتان. وكل واحدة منهما مقولة بالقياس إلى الأخرى وقد ثبت : أن المضافين يوجدان معاً في الأعيان وفي الأذهان . فلو كانا موجودين ، لوجب أن معاً يوجدا ، ولو وجدا معاً ، لحصل معروضاهما معاً ، ضرورة أن الإضافة لا توجد وحدها ، بل إنما توجد عند وجود موصوفها ومعروضها ، وحينئذ يلزم أن يقال : والبعد يوجب كونها موجودين معاً فيلزم أن يقال : الشيء من حيث هو قبل غيره ، يجب أن يكون موجوداً معه ، وهو محال . الرابع : أن نقول : لما ثبت أن المضافين يوجدان معاً ، فهذه المعية إن كانت وصفاً زائداً عليهما ، كان ذلك الزائد أيضاً معهما ، فتكون هذه المعية الثانية زائدة ، ولزم التسلسل . وإن لم يكن وصفاً زائداً ، فلم لا يجوز مثله في سائر المعيات والقبليات ؟ لا يقال : إن كون المضافين معاً ، نفس ذاتيهما . لأنـا نقول : إذا قلنا : المضافان يوجدان معاً ، فهو قضية موضوعها : قولنا المضافان . ومحمولها قولنا يوجدان معاً. والمحمول في كل قضية غير الموضوع لامتناع حمل الشيء الواحد بالاعتبار الواحد على نفسه . وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه يبطل هذا العذر . فثبت بهذه الوجه : أن القبلية والبعدية لا يمكن أن يكونا من الصفات الموجودة في الأعيان
Then we say: That which indicates that priority and posteriority cannot be among existing things are aspects: The first: Indeed, plain reason judges that every originated thing is preceded by its non-existence, and that its non-existence is prior to its existence. This necessitates that priority, precedence, and being earlier are attributes of non-existence, and whatever is an attribute of non-existence is impossible to be an existent attribute, because of the impossibility of an existent attribute subsisting in pure non-existence and pure negation. So it is established that priority and posteriority are not among existent attributes. The second: If priority were an existent attribute, then that existent attribute, in relation to other than itself, would either be prior, simultaneous, or posterior, and an infinite regress would follow. It cannot be said: Why is it not permissible that priority, in relation to other than itself, even if it is prior, yet its being so is identical to its essence, not an additional attribute to the essence? Because we say: When we judge that priority is prior to something else, here the essence of priority is the subject, then we judge that it is prior to something else which is the predicate, and the predicate of a proposition is necessarily other than its subject. So it is established that if priority were an existent attribute, its being prior in relation to something else would be impossible for it to be identical to its essence, but it must be something different from its essence. The third: Indeed, priority and posteriority are two relations. Each one of them is predicated relative to the other, and it has been established that the two relatives exist together in external objects and in minds. So if they were existent, they would necessarily exist together, and if they existed together, their subjects would occur together, necessarily because a relation does not exist alone, but only exists when its described thing and its subject exist. Then it would be necessary to say: Posteriority necessitates that they exist together, so it would be necessary to say: A thing, insofar as it is prior to another, must exist with it, which is impossible. The fourth: We say: Since it is established that the two relatives exist together, so this togetherness, if it is an additional attribute to them, then that additional thing would also be with them, so this second togetherness would be additional, and an infinite regress would follow. And if it is not an additional attribute, then why is the like of this not permissible in all other togethernesses and priorities? It cannot be said: That the two relatives togetherness is identical to their essences, because we say: When we say 'the two relatives exist together', it is a proposition whose subject is our saying 'the two relatives', and its predicate is our saying 'exist together', and the predicate in every proposition is other than the subject, due to the impossibility of predicating one thing by one consideration upon itself. And upon this supposition, this excuse is invalidated. So it is established by this aspect that priority and posteriority cannot be among the existent attributes in external objects.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage presents four independent proofs (wujuh) demonstrating that priority (qabliyya) and posteriority (ba'diyya) are not existent attributes (sifat mawjuda) in external reality. The author's overarching claim is that these temporal relations are not real properties inhering in things. First proof: Plain reason tells us that every originated thing is preceded by its non-existence; thus priority is an attribute of non-existence, and an existent attribute cannot subsist in pure non-existence. Therefore priority and posteriority are not existent attributes. Second proof: If priority were an existent attribute, it would itself relate to other things as prior, simultaneous, or posterior, leading to infinite regress. The author refutes a potential objection that priority's being prior might be identical to its essence, by analyzing the propositional structure: the subject (essence of priority) and predicate (being prior to something) are distinct, so the relation is additional, not identical. Third proof: Priority and posteriority are relational concepts (idafatan); relatives exist together. If they were existent, they would have to exist simultaneously, but then a prior thing would exist with its posterior, which is impossible. Fourth proof: Relatives exist together. If the togetherness is an additional attribute, it leads to regress; if not, why not allow similar togetherness in all cases? The author rejects the claim that togetherness is identical to essences by again appealing to the subject-predicate distinction in propositions. Thus all four proofs conclude that priority and posteriority are not real attributes in external objects (a'yan).

Key Terms
قبلية
بعدية
صفة موجودة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Priority and posteriority are real attributes that inhere in things like whiteness.
Correction: The author shows that priority is an attribute of non-existence, so it cannot be a real, existent attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why can priority not be an existent attribute?
A) Because priority is a relation, and relations cannot exist.
B) Because priority is an attribute of non-existence, and an existent attribute cannot inhere in non-existence.
C) Because priority leads to infinite regress.
D) Because priority and posteriority must exist together.

Key Takeaway
Priority is not an existent attribute because it describes non-existence, and an existent attribute cannot inhere in non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever treated something that is merely a relation of non-existence (like 'before') as if it were a real thing? How might this affect your understanding of Allah's attributes?
?
If priority is not an existent attribute, then what does it mean to say 'Allah existed before creation'? How does this passage refine your understanding of that statement?
?
This proof relies on the impossibility of an existent attribute in pure non-existence. Is there any area of your faith where you have imagined a quality subsisting in nothing? Repent from that assumption.

Second Proof: Infinite Regress Argument
Second proof: regress from assuming priority is existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why priority cannot be an existent attribute because it would lead to infinite regress and the predicate is distinct from the subject.

Core Idea
If priority were existent, it would need another priority, causing regress.

The second proof takes a different approach: assuming priority is an existent attribute, it must relate to other things. This relation would itself require explanation, leading to an infinite chain. The author also refutes a potential objection by analyzing propositional structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full argument. Notice how the author sets up the conditional statement and responds to an objection.
2
Understand the regress argument
If priority is existent, then it is either prior, simultaneous, or posterior to other things. Each option leads to regress or contradiction.
The author focuses on the case where it is prior.
3
Analyze the objection and response
The objection claims that priority's being prior might be identical to its essence. The author refutes by distinguishing subject and predicate in a proposition.
This is a key logical move.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : الذي يدل على أن القبلية والبعدية لا يمكن أن يكونا من الأمور الموجودة : وجوه : الأول : إن صريح العقل يحكم بأن كل محدث ، فإنه مسبوق بعدمه ، وأن عدمه سابق على وجوده. وهذا يقتضي كون القبلية والسبق والتقدم وصفاً للعدم ، وما كان وصفاً للعدم ، امتنع أن يكون صفة موجودة ، لامتناع قيام الصفة الموجودة بالمعدوم المحض والنفي الصرف. فثبت : أن القبلية والبعدية ليست من الصفات الموجودة . الثاني : لو كانت القبلية صفة موجودة ، لكانت تلك الصفة الموجودة بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، إما أن تكون قبلاً أو معاً أو بعداً ، ويلزم التسلسل . لا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن تكون القبلية بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، وإن كانت قبلاً ، إلا أن كونها كذلك عين ذاته. لا أنه صفة زائدة على الذات ؟ لأنا نقول : إذا حكمنا على القبلية بأنها قبل شيء آخر ، فههنا ذات القبلية هي الموضوع . ثم حكمنا عليها بأنها قبل شيء آخر هو المحمول ، ومحمول القضية غير موضوعها لا محالة . فثبت : أن القبلية لو كانت صفة موجودة لكان كونها قبلاً بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، يمتنع أن يكون عين ذاتها ، بل لا بد وأن يكون أمراً مغايراً لذاتها . الثالث : إن القبلية والبعدية إضافتان. وكل واحدة منهما مقولة بالقياس إلى الأخرى وقد ثبت : أن المضافين يوجدان معاً في الأعيان وفي الأذهان . فلو كانا موجودين ، لوجب أن معاً يوجدا ، ولو وجدا معاً ، لحصل معروضاهما معاً ، ضرورة أن الإضافة لا توجد وحدها ، بل إنما توجد عند وجود موصوفها ومعروضها ، وحينئذ يلزم أن يقال : والبعد يوجب كونها موجودين معاً فيلزم أن يقال : الشيء من حيث هو قبل غيره ، يجب أن يكون موجوداً معه ، وهو محال . الرابع : أن نقول : لما ثبت أن المضافين يوجدان معاً ، فهذه المعية إن كانت وصفاً زائداً عليهما ، كان ذلك الزائد أيضاً معهما ، فتكون هذه المعية الثانية زائدة ، ولزم التسلسل . وإن لم يكن وصفاً زائداً ، فلم لا يجوز مثله في سائر المعيات والقبليات ؟ لا يقال : إن كون المضافين معاً ، نفس ذاتيهما . لأنـا نقول : إذا قلنا : المضافان يوجدان معاً ، فهو قضية موضوعها : قولنا المضافان . ومحمولها قولنا يوجدان معاً. والمحمول في كل قضية غير الموضوع لامتناع حمل الشيء الواحد بالاعتبار الواحد على نفسه . وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه يبطل هذا العذر . فثبت بهذه الوجه : أن القبلية والبعدية لا يمكن أن يكونا من الصفات الموجودة في الأعيان

This necessitates that priority, precedence, and being earlier are attributes of non-existence, and whatever is an attribute of non-existence is impossible to be an existent attribute, because of the impossibility of an existent attribute subsisting in pure non-existence and pure negation. Commentary
This passage presents four independent proofs (wujuh) demonstrating that priority (qabliyya) and posteriority (ba'diyya) are not existent attributes (sifat mawjuda) in external reality. The author's overarching claim is that these temporal relations are not real properties inhering in things. First proof: Plain reason tells us that every originated thing is preceded by its non-existence; thus priority is an attribute of non-existence, and an existent attribute cannot subsist in pure non-existence. Therefore priority and posteriority are not existent attributes. Second proof: If priority were an existent attribute, it would itself relate to other things as prior, simultaneous, or posterior, leading to infinite regress. The author refutes a potential objection that priority's being prior might be identical to its essence, by analyzing the propositional structure: the subject (essence of priority) and predicate (being prior to something) are distinct, so the relation is additional, not identical. Third proof: Priority and posteriority are relational concepts (idafatan); relatives exist together. If they were existent, they would have to exist simultaneously, but then a prior thing would exist with its posterior, which is impossible. Fourth proof: Relatives exist together. If the togetherness is an additional attribute, it leads to regress; if not, why not allow similar togetherness in all cases? The author rejects the claim that togetherness is identical to essences by again appealing to the subject-predicate distinction in propositions. Thus all four proofs conclude that priority and posteriority are not real attributes in external objects (a'yan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Priority could be an existent attribute that is self-referential without regress.
Correction: The argument shows that if priority were existent, its relation to others would require an additional attribute, causing regress.

Checkpoint
What is the key logical principle used to refute the objection in the second proof?
A) The principle of non-contradiction.
B) The predicate of a proposition is necessarily distinct from the subject.
C) Infinite regress is impossible.
D) Priority and posteriority are relational.

Key Takeaway
If priority were an existent attribute, it would require an additional relation to be prior, leading to infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this lesson, you saw that assuming priority is an existent attribute leads to a logical contradiction. Now think: are there beliefs or habits in your life that you treat as 'essential' to your identity, when in fact they are mere relations that could lead to endless self-justification? Will you dare to examine one such belief today and see if it withstands the same logical scrutiny?
?
The author's response hinges on the distinction between subject and predicate—between what something is and what is said about it. Where have you conflated your own essence with a quality you possess, perhaps thinking you cannot change? What would it cost you to separate the two and admit that quality is not you, but an attribute you could let go?
?
If priority cannot be an existent attribute because it would require infinite regress, what does that reveal about your own need to be 'first' or 'prior' in the eyes of others? Are you chasing a status that, if actualized, would only demand more, never ending? Will you repent from that pursuit and find your worth in Allah alone?

Third Proof: Relational Nature and Simultaneity
Third proof: relational nature forces simultaneity, contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why priority and posteriority cannot be existent because they are relations that would require simultaneous existence, which is absurd.

Core Idea
Priority and posteriority are relational; relatives exist together, so a prior would need to exist with its posterior.

The third proof draws on the nature of relations (iḍāfa). Priority and posteriority are correlatives: each is defined relative to the other. Since correlatives exist simultaneously, if they were real attributes, they would have to exist together, but a prior thing cannot coexist with its posterior in the same moment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read carefully. The argument hinges on the concept of 'iḍāfa' (relation) and the principle that relatives exist together.
2
Understand the relational nature
Priority and posteriority are a pair of relatives. Each is only meaningful relative to the other.
3
Apply the simultaneity principle
Relatives exist at the same time. If priority and posteriority were real, they would have to coexist, but that would mean a prior thing exists at the same time as a posterior thing, which is contradictory.
Note the phrase 'واجتمعا معا'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : الذي يدل على أن القبلية والبعدية لا يمكن أن يكونا من الأمور الموجودة : وجوه : الأول : إن صريح العقل يحكم بأن كل محدث ، فإنه مسبوق بعدمه ، وأن عدمه سابق على وجوده. وهذا يقتضي كون القبلية والسبق والتقدم وصفاً للعدم ، وما كان وصفاً للعدم ، امتنع أن يكون صفة موجودة ، لامتناع قيام الصفة الموجودة بالمعدوم المحض والنفي الصرف. فثبت : أن القبلية والبعدية ليست من الصفات الموجودة . الثاني : لو كانت القبلية صفة موجودة ، لكانت تلك الصفة الموجودة بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، إما أن تكون قبلاً أو معاً أو بعداً ، ويلزم التسلسل . لا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن تكون القبلية بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، وإن كانت قبلاً ، إلا أن كونها كذلك عين ذاته. لا أنه صفة زائدة على الذات ؟ لأنا نقول : إذا حكمنا على القبلية بأنها قبل شيء آخر ، فههنا ذات القبلية هي الموضوع . ثم حكمنا عليها بأنها قبل شيء آخر هو المحمول ، ومحمول القضية غير موضوعها لا محالة . فثبت : أن القبلية لو كانت صفة موجودة لكان كونها قبلاً بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، يمتنع أن يكون عين ذاتها ، بل لا بد وأن يكون أمراً مغايراً لذاتها . الثالث : إن القبلية والبعدية إضافتان. وكل واحدة منهما مقولة بالقياس إلى الأخرى وقد ثبت : أن المضافين يوجدان معاً في الأعيان وفي الأذهان . فلو كانا موجودين ، لوجب أن معاً يوجدا ، ولو وجدا معاً ، لحصل معروضاهما معاً ، ضرورة أن الإضافة لا توجد وحدها ، بل إنما توجد عند وجود موصوفها ومعروضها ، وحينئذ يلزم أن يقال : والبعد يوجب كونها موجودين معاً فيلزم أن يقال : الشيء من حيث هو قبل غيره ، يجب أن يكون موجوداً معه ، وهو محال . الرابع : أن نقول : لما ثبت أن المضافين يوجدان معاً ، فهذه المعية إن كانت وصفاً زائداً عليهما ، كان ذلك الزائد أيضاً معهما ، فتكون هذه المعية الثانية زائدة ، ولزم التسلسل . وإن لم يكن وصفاً زائداً ، فلم لا يجوز مثله في سائر المعيات والقبليات ؟ لا يقال : إن كون المضافين معاً ، نفس ذاتيهما . لأنـا نقول : إذا قلنا : المضافان يوجدان معاً ، فهو قضية موضوعها : قولنا المضافان . ومحمولها قولنا يوجدان معاً. والمحمول في كل قضية غير الموضوع لامتناع حمل الشيء الواحد بالاعتبار الواحد على نفسه . وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه يبطل هذا العذر . فثبت بهذه الوجه : أن القبلية والبعدية لا يمكن أن يكونا من الصفات الموجودة في الأعيان
Then we say: That which indicates that priority and posteriority cannot be among existing things are aspects: The first: Indeed, plain reason judges that every originated thing is preceded by its non-existence, and that its non-existence is prior to its existence. This necessitates that priority, precedence, and being earlier are attributes of non-existence, and whatever is an attribute of non-existence is impossible to be an existent attribute, because of the impossibility of an existent attribute subsisting in pure non-existence and pure negation. So it is established that priority and posteriority are not among existent attributes. The second: If priority were an existent attribute, then that existent attribute, in relation to other than itself, would either be prior, simultaneous, or posterior, and an infinite regress would follow. It cannot be said: Why is it not permissible that priority, in relation to other than itself, even if it is prior, yet its being so is identical to its essence, not an additional attribute to the essence? Because we say: When we judge that priority is prior to something else, here the essence of priority is the subject, then we judge that it is prior to something else which is the predicate, and the predicate of a proposition is necessarily other than its subject. So it is established that if priority were an existent attribute, its being prior in relation to something else would be impossible for it to be identical to its essence, but it must be something different from its essence. The third: Indeed, priority and posteriority are two relations. Each one of them is predicated relative to the other, and it has been established that the two relatives exist together in external objects and in minds. So if they were existent, they would necessarily exist together, and if they existed together, their subjects would occur together, necessarily because a relation does not exist alone, but only exists when its described thing and its subject exist. Then it would be necessary to say: Posteriority necessitates that they exist together, so it would be necessary to say: A thing, insofar as it is prior to another, must exist with it, which is impossible. The fourth: We say: Since it is established that the two relatives exist together, so this togetherness, if it is an additional attribute to them, then that additional thing would also be with them, so this second togetherness would be additional, and an infinite regress would follow. And if it is not an additional attribute, then why is the like of this not permissible in all other togethernesses and priorities? It cannot be said: That the two relatives togetherness is identical to their essences, because we say: When we say 'the two relatives exist together', it is a proposition whose subject is our saying 'the two relatives', and its predicate is our saying 'exist together', and the predicate in every proposition is other than the subject, due to the impossibility of predicating one thing by one consideration upon itself. And upon this supposition, this excuse is invalidated. So it is established by this aspect that priority and posteriority cannot be among the existent attributes in external objects.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage presents four independent proofs (wujuh) demonstrating that priority (qabliyya) and posteriority (ba'diyya) are not existent attributes (sifat mawjuda) in external reality. The author's overarching claim is that these temporal relations are not real properties inhering in things. First proof: Plain reason tells us that every originated thing is preceded by its non-existence; thus priority is an attribute of non-existence, and an existent attribute cannot subsist in pure non-existence. Therefore priority and posteriority are not existent attributes. Second proof: If priority were an existent attribute, it would itself relate to other things as prior, simultaneous, or posterior, leading to infinite regress. The author refutes a potential objection that priority's being prior might be identical to its essence, by analyzing the propositional structure: the subject (essence of priority) and predicate (being prior to something) are distinct, so the relation is additional, not identical. Third proof: Priority and posteriority are relational concepts (idafatan); relatives exist together. If they were existent, they would have to exist simultaneously, but then a prior thing would exist with its posterior, which is impossible. Fourth proof: Relatives exist together. If the togetherness is an additional attribute, it leads to regress; if not, why not allow similar togetherness in all cases? The author rejects the claim that togetherness is identical to essences by again appealing to the subject-predicate distinction in propositions. Thus all four proofs conclude that priority and posteriority are not real attributes in external objects (a'yan).

Key Terms
قبلية
بعدية
إضافة
معية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Priority and posteriority can be real attributes like any other property.
Correction: They are relational and would require simultaneous existence of prior and posterior, which is contradictory.

Checkpoint
What is the key principle used in the third proof?
A) Infinite regress is impossible.
B) Relatives exist together.
C) Essence and attribute are distinct.
D) Priority is an attribute of non-existence.

Key Takeaway
Priority and posteriority are relational; if real, they would force simultaneous existence, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often think of your own actions as 'before' or 'after' other events. This lesson shows that such priority and posteriority are mere relations, not real attributes of those actions. How does that change the way you view your past mistakes and future hopes? Are you willing to see them as interconnected rather than separate, and what would that mean for your repentance or planning?
?
Consider the belief that God's attribute of 'being First' (al-Awwal) is a real attribute. This proof denies that priority can be a real attribute. Does that trouble you? How do you reconcile the lesson's conclusion with the Islamic name 'al-Awwal'? This is not a question of knowledge, but of heart: are you willing to submit to the logic even if it challenges a comfortable understanding? What do you need to investigate further?

Fourth Proof: Regress from Togetherness
Fourth proof: regress from togetherness attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof that priority and posteriority cannot be existent because their togetherness either leads to infinite regress or is not an attribute.

Core Idea
If relatives exist together, the togetherness itself raises a regress or must be essential.

The fourth proof builds on the previous insight that relatives exist together. It then examines the status of this 'togetherness' (ma‘iyya). If togetherness is an additional attribute, it leads to regress; if it is identical to their essences, then why can't priority itself be essential? The author resolves this by again using the subject-predicate distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full argument. Notice how the author presents two options for the togetherness and refutes the objection.
2
Understand the two options for togetherness
Either togetherness is an additional attribute (leads to regress) or identical to essences (then why not allow the same for priority?).
3
Analyze the refutation of the second option
The objection claims togetherness is identical to essences. The author shows that in the proposition 'the two relatives exist together', the predicate is distinct from the subject, so togetherness cannot be identical to essences.
This mirrors the logic used in the second proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : الذي يدل على أن القبلية والبعدية لا يمكن أن يكونا من الأمور الموجودة : وجوه : الأول : إن صريح العقل يحكم بأن كل محدث ، فإنه مسبوق بعدمه ، وأن عدمه سابق على وجوده. وهذا يقتضي كون القبلية والسبق والتقدم وصفاً للعدم ، وما كان وصفاً للعدم ، امتنع أن يكون صفة موجودة ، لامتناع قيام الصفة الموجودة بالمعدوم المحض والنفي الصرف. فثبت : أن القبلية والبعدية ليست من الصفات الموجودة . الثاني : لو كانت القبلية صفة موجودة ، لكانت تلك الصفة الموجودة بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، إما أن تكون قبلاً أو معاً أو بعداً ، ويلزم التسلسل . لا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن تكون القبلية بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، وإن كانت قبلاً ، إلا أن كونها كذلك عين ذاته. لا أنه صفة زائدة على الذات ؟ لأنا نقول : إذا حكمنا على القبلية بأنها قبل شيء آخر ، فههنا ذات القبلية هي الموضوع . ثم حكمنا عليها بأنها قبل شيء آخر هو المحمول ، ومحمول القضية غير موضوعها لا محالة . فثبت : أن القبلية لو كانت صفة موجودة لكان كونها قبلاً بالنسبة إلى غيرها ، يمتنع أن يكون عين ذاتها ، بل لا بد وأن يكون أمراً مغايراً لذاتها . الثالث : إن القبلية والبعدية إضافتان. وكل واحدة منهما مقولة بالقياس إلى الأخرى وقد ثبت : أن المضافين يوجدان معاً في الأعيان وفي الأذهان . فلو كانا موجودين ، لوجب أن معاً يوجدا ، ولو وجدا معاً ، لحصل معروضاهما معاً ، ضرورة أن الإضافة لا توجد وحدها ، بل إنما توجد عند وجود موصوفها ومعروضها ، وحينئذ يلزم أن يقال : والبعد يوجب كونها موجودين معاً فيلزم أن يقال : الشيء من حيث هو قبل غيره ، يجب أن يكون موجوداً معه ، وهو محال . الرابع : أن نقول : لما ثبت أن المضافين يوجدان معاً ، فهذه المعية إن كانت وصفاً زائداً عليهما ، كان ذلك الزائد أيضاً معهما ، فتكون هذه المعية الثانية زائدة ، ولزم التسلسل . وإن لم يكن وصفاً زائداً ، فلم لا يجوز مثله في سائر المعيات والقبليات ؟ لا يقال : إن كون المضافين معاً ، نفس ذاتيهما . لأنـا نقول : إذا قلنا : المضافان يوجدان معاً ، فهو قضية موضوعها : قولنا المضافان . ومحمولها قولنا يوجدان معاً. والمحمول في كل قضية غير الموضوع لامتناع حمل الشيء الواحد بالاعتبار الواحد على نفسه . وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه يبطل هذا العذر . فثبت بهذه الوجه : أن القبلية والبعدية لا يمكن أن يكونا من الصفات الموجودة في الأعيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The togetherness of relatives can be an essential property without regress.
Correction: The author shows that no property can be predicated of a thing and be identical to its essence, as the predicate must be distinct.

Checkpoint
In the fourth proof, what happens if togetherness is an additional attribute?
A) It becomes identical to the essence.
B) It leads to infinite regress.
C) It proves priority is existent.
D) It is impossible by definition.

Key Takeaway
The togetherness of relatives cannot be an additional attribute without regress, nor can it be identical to essences, thus priority and posteriority are not real attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If priority and posteriority are not real attributes in external objects, then your sense of time—before and after—is not a fixed, objective reality but a relation you impose on things. How does that change the way you view your past mistakes and future hopes? Are you willing to release the grip of 'before' and 'after' as if they define your worth?
?
The proof shows that even togetherness cannot be a real additional attribute without leading to regress. Think about your deepest relationships: do you treat them as extra 'things' you possess, or as essential to who you are? What would it mean to see them as essential rather than add-ons?

The Objection That Time Is a Distinct Cause and Its Refutation
Refutation of the objection that time is distinct from motion's measure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-fold refutation of the claim that time is a distinct cause of motion's measure, and why this refutation is crucial for defending the definition of time as the measure of motion.

Core Idea
The objector first claims time is the measure of motion, then calls it a cause—contradiction.

This passage presents a typical kalam objection followed by a crisp two-part refutation. The author shows that the objector contradicts his own definition, and then demonstrates that his alternative leads to identifying time with God, an absurdity. Understanding this refutation sharpens one's grasp of the nature of time and causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and refutation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: objection followed by 'we say: This is refuted from two aspects'.
The objector tries to separate time from the measure of motion.
2
Identify the two refutation points
The author explicitly lists two refutations. Find the phrases 'الوجه الأول' and 'الوجه الثاني' in the Arabic. These correspond to the two arguments.
Each refutation stands independently.
3
Analyze the first refutation
The first refutation shows that the objector abandons his original position. He initially said time is the measure of motion, but now says it is a meaning that necessitates the measure. This is a contradiction.
Ask yourself: Is the objector consistent?
4
Analyze the second refutation
The second refutation argues that if time is the cause of the measure of motion, and motion is a possible existent whose duration depends on its cause, then time must be the necessarily existent First Cause—which is false.
This argument uses the principle of causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : هذا الكلام إنما يلزم ، إذا قلنا : الزمان نفس مقدار الحركة، ونحن لا نقول بذلك بل نقول إن لكل واحد من الحركات مقدار خاص بها على حدة . وههنا شيء آخر مباين عن الكل، هو المقتضى لحصول تلك المقادير، وذلك الشيء هو الزمان . فنقول : هذا مدفوع من وجهين : الأول : إن مذهبكم أنه لا حقيقة للزمان إلا مقدار الحركة، فلما أبطلنا عليكم هذا الكلام، تركتم في هذا السؤال ذلك المذهب، وقلتم : الزمان عبارة عن المعنى المقتضي لمقدار الحركة، ومن المعلوم أنه فرق بين مقدار الحركة وبين المعنى المقتضي لمقدار الحركة. فإن قلتم : الزمان معنى يقتضي مقدار الحركة، كان هذا تركا لقولكم : إن الزمان هو مقدار الحركة . والوجه الثاني في دفع هذا الكلام : هو أنا قلنا : إنه لا معنى لمقدار حركة الفلك، إلا امتداد دوامها وامتدادها . ومعلوم أن دوام الشيء الذي يكون ممكن الوجود لا يكون إلا لدوام علته الموجدة له، فيلزمكم على قولكم أن تقولوا : إن الزمان عبارة عن الموجود الواجب لذاته الذي هو السبب الأول والعلة الأولى . وذلك باطل . والله أعلم
For if someone says: This argument only follows if we say that time is the very measure of motion, but we do not say that; rather we say that each motion has its own measure separately. And here there is something else distinct from all, which is the cause of the occurrence of those measures, and that thing is time. So we say: This is refuted from two aspects: First: Your position is that time has no reality except as the measure of motion. When we invalidated this statement for you, you abandoned that position in this question and said: Time is the meaning that necessitates the measure of motion. It is known that there is a difference between the measure of motion and the meaning that necessitates the measure of motion. If you say time is a meaning that necessitates the measure of motion, then this is abandoning your statement that time is the measure of motion. The second aspect in repelling this statement: We said that there is no meaning to the measure of the motion of the sphere except the extension of its duration and its extension. It is known that the duration of a thing that is possible in existence only exists due to the duration of its efficient cause. According to your statement, you must say that time is the necessarily existent being who is the first cause and the first agent. That is false. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its two refutations. The objector argues that if time were the measure of motion, then many times would occur simultaneously, but instead he claims time is a distinct cause of the measures. The author refutes in two ways. First, the objector contradicts his own original position that time is merely the measure of motion; by calling time a 'meaning that necessitates the measure,' he abandons his original claim. Second, the objector's position leads to an absurd consequence: if time is the cause of the duration of motion, which is a possible existent, then time must be the necessarily existent First Cause (God), which is false because time is contingent. Thus the objection fails.

Key Terms
الزمان
الحركة
مقدار الحركة
المعنى المقتضي
الموجود الواجب لذاته
العلة الأولى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the objector presents a coherent alternative definition of time as a distinct cause.
Correction: The objector's position is self-contradictory because he originally defined time as the measure of motion, and his new definition abandons that. Additionally, his view leads to identifying time with God, which is false.

Checkpoint
What is the first refutation against the objector's claim that time is a distinct meaning that necessitates the measure of motion?
A) It leads to a contradiction because time would then be the measure of motion after all.
B) The objector abandons his original position that time is the measure of motion.
C) The objector's claim implies that time is the necessarily existent being.
D) The objector fails to define motion properly.

Key Takeaway
The objector's claim that time is a distinct cause of measures fails because it contradicts his own definition and leads to identifying time with God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a belief, do you ever unconsciously shift its definition when challenged, just like the objector? Take a moment to examine your own convictions: is there a truth you have redefined to avoid its implications? Commit to consistency even when it costs you.
?
This passage shows that if time were the cause of motion's duration, it would have to be God. Does your understanding of time reflect its contingency, or do you sometimes treat time as an independent force? How can you remind yourself that only Allah is the true Cause?
?
The refutation identifies a contradiction in the objector's position. Are you willing to let the truth expose contradictions in your own thinking, even if it means abandoning a comfortable idea? Set aside one belief today that does not withstand honest scrutiny.

Second Proof: Extension of Motion Has No External Existence
Author argues the extension of motion lacks external existence, so its measure cannot be time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the extension of motion lacks external existence, and why this entails that time cannot be its measure.

Core Idea
The extension of motion is a mental abstraction; only discrete moments exist externally.

This passage presents the second proof against identifying time with the measure of motion. The author first clarifies what 'measure of motion' means, then demonstrates that the extension of motion has no external existence. He responds to an objection and concludes that since time does exist externally, it cannot be the measure of motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the full flow of the argument. Notice how the author structures his proof with an objection and response.
2
Identify the core claim
Find where the author states that 'the extension of motion has no existence in external reality.' This is the pivotal point.
3
Follow the demonstration
The author shows that motion consists of successive discrete occurrences, not a continuous whole. Understand why this means the extension is not an external existent.
4
Examine the objection and response
An objector argues that motion is a continuous state. The author replies that only each specific occurrence exists externally, not the continuous span.
5
Understand the conclusion
Since the extension does not exist externally, its measure—an attribute—cannot exist either. The known external existence of time then forces the conclusion that time is not the measure of motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية في إبطال قول من يقول : الزمان عبارة عن مقدار حركة أن نقول : إنا قد ذكرنا أنه لا يعقل من قولنا : الزمان مقدار الحركة، إلا أنه مقدار امتداد الحركة. إذا عرفت هذا. فنقول : امتداد الحركة لا وجود له في الأعيان، وإذا كان كذلك، امتنع أن يكون مقدار ذلك الامتداد أمراً موجوداً في الأعيان، أما بيان أن امتداد الحركة لا وجود له في الأعيان فهو أن الحركة عبارة عن حصولات متعاقبة في أحياز معاقبة، ومن المعلوم بالبديهة أنه لا وجود لمجموع تلك الحصولات في الأعيان، وإنما الموجود منها حصول واحد في آن واحد، ثم ينقضي ويحصل بعده مثله . فثبت : أن امتداد الحركة لا وجود له في الأعيان . فإن قالوا : الحركة عبارة عن كون الجسم متوسطاً بين المبدأ والمنتهى، بحيث لا يكون حاله في آن من الآنات المفروضة في تلك المدة مشابهاً لحاله قبل ذلك ولا بعده، وهذه الحالة باقية مستمرة . وذلك يدل على أن امتداد الحركة أمر موجود في الأعيان فنقول : الذي يحصل في الأعيان هو الحصول في هذا المعين، ثم في حد آخر معين . وهكذا على التعاقب والتوالي، وذلك يدل على أن امتداد الحركة لا حصول له في الأعيان، وأما بيان أنه متى كان الأمر كذلك، امتنع أن يكون لمقدار ذلك الامتداد وجود في الأعيان، فالدليل عليه : ان مقدار هذا الامتداد صفة من صفات هذا الامتداد، والموصوف إذا كان ممتنع الوجود في الأعيان، فالصفة أولى بأن تكون ممتنعة الوجود في الأعيان، فثبت بهذا الذي بيناه : أن مقدار الحركة يمتنع أن يكون موجوداً في الأعيان . لكن الشيخ بين بالدلائل : أن الزمان موجود في الأعيان . ينتج أنه لا شيء من الزمان عبارة عن مقدار الحركة .
The second proof in invalidating the statement of whoever says that time is the measure of motion: We say: We have mentioned that from our statement 'time is the measure of motion' nothing is understood except that it is the measure of the extension of motion. If you know this, we say: The extension of motion has no existence in external reality. If this is so, it is impossible that the measure of that extension be something existing in external reality. As for the demonstration that the extension of motion has no existence in external reality: Motion consists of successive occurrences in consecutive places. It is known intuitively that the totality of those occurrences has no existence in external reality; rather, only one occurrence exists at one moment, then it passes and another similar one occurs after it. So it is established that the extension of motion has no existence in external reality. If they say: Motion is the body being intermediate between the starting point and the endpoint, such that its state in any of the assumed moments of that period is not similar to its state before or after, and this state is lasting and continuous. This indicates that the extension of motion is something existing in external reality. We say: What obtains in external reality is the occurrence in this particular point, then in another particular point, and so on consecutively and successively. That indicates that the extension of motion has no occurrence in external reality. As for the demonstration that when this is the case, it is impossible for the measure of that extension to have existence in external reality: The evidence for it is that the measure of this extension is an attribute of this extension, and if the described is impossible of existence in external reality, then the attribute is even more deserving of being impossible of existence in external reality. So it is established by what we have clarified that the measure of motion is impossible to exist in external reality. But the sheikh has demonstrated with proofs that time exists in external reality. It follows that none of time is the measure of motion.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof against identifying time with the measure of motion. The author first clarifies that 'measure of motion' means 'measure of the extension of motion.' He then argues that the extension of motion has no external existence because motion consists of discrete occurrences, not a continuous whole. An objection is raised: motion is a continuous state of being intermediate between start and end. The author answers that what exists externally is only each specific occurrence, not a continuous extension. Since the extension does not exist externally, its measure—an attribute of that extension—cannot exist externally either. Because time is known to exist externally, time cannot be the measure of motion.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The extension of motion is a real continuous entity that exists in the external world.
Correction: The extension of motion is merely a mental abstraction from a series of discrete occurrences; only each individual occurrence exists externally, one at a time.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Time cannot be the measure of motion because the extension of motion—which that measure would quantify—does not exist in external reality.
